2:24:1487:0:14:72:365:700:12:Times:12:g_d0_f1:The Optimal Use of Government Purchases for Stabilization 
2:25:1544:14:14:72:256:686:12:Times:12:Times:Pascal Michaillat and Emmanuel Saez
2:26:1579:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:NBER Working Paper No. 21322
2:27:1607:14:14:72:232:658:12:Times:12:g_d0_f2:July 2015, Revised October 2016
2:28:1638:14:28:72:204:644:12:Times:12:Times:JEL No. E32,E62,H21,H41
2:29:1661:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:ABSTRACT
2:30:1669:28:14:72:546:588:12:Times:12:Times:This   paper   describes   the   optimal   level   of   government   purchases   in   the   presence   of 
2:31:1775:14:14:72:546:574:12:Times:12:Times:unemployment. The  theoretical  framework  is  a  general-equilibrium  matching  model  in  which 
2:32:1872:14:14:71:545:560:12:Times:12:Times:government  purchases are  valuable.  When  the  unemployment  gap  is  zero,  the  conventional 
2:33:1968:14:14:71:546:546:12:Times:12:Times:Samuelson   formula   is   valid.   Otherwise, optimal   government   spending   deviates   from   the 
2:34:2070:14:14:72:545:532:12:Times:12:Times:Samuelson  level  to  fill  the  unemployment  gap  partially. Hence,  with  a  positive  unemployment 
2:35:2172:14:14:72:545:518:12:Times:12:Times:multiplier   (so   that   increasing   government   purchases   reduces unemployment),   government 
2:36:2271:14:14:72:545:504:12:Times:12:Times:spending should be higher than the Samuelson level when unemployment is inefficiently high and 
2:37:2365:14:14:72:546:490:12:Times:12:Times:lower  when  unemployment  is  inefficiently  low.  We  characterize  the  optimal level  of  stimulus 
2:38:2467:14:14:72:545:476:12:Times:12:Times:spending.  We  find  that  stimulus  spending  is  largest  for  a  moderate  unemployment multiplier. 
2:39:2569:14:14:72:545:462:12:Times:12:Times:With larger multipliers, stimulus spending is smaller because less spending is required to fill the 
2:40:2668:14:14:72:546:448:12:Times:12:Times:unemployment gap. With smaller multipliers, stimulus spending is smaller because there is more 
2:41:2762:14:14:72:546:434:12:Times:12:Times:crowding  out  of  private  spending  by  public  spending.  We  also  find  that  stimulus  spending 
2:42:2864:14:14:72:545:420:12:Times:12:Times:increases with the elasticity of substitution between public and private consumption. With a zero 
2:43:2961:14:14:72:546:406:12:Times:12:Times:elasticity (so that additional public workers dig and fill holes), stimulus spending is zero. With an 
2:44:3062:14:14:71:546:392:12:Times:12:Times:infinite elasticity (so that private and public workers are perfect substitute), stimulus spending is 
2:45:3163:14:14:72:545:378:12:Times:12:Times:large enough to fill the unemployment gap completely. Finally, the results hold whether taxes are 
2:46:3260:14:42:71:231:364:12:Times:12:Times:nondistortionary or distortionary.
2:47:3294:42:14:71:154:322:12:Times:12:Times:Pascal Michaillat
2:48:3311:14:14:71:197:308:12:Times:12:Times:Department of Economics
2:49:3334:14:14:71:160:294:12:Times:12:Times: Brown University
2:50:3351:14:14:71:242:280:12:Times:12:Times:http://pascalmichaillat.weebly.com/
2:51:3386:14:28:71:217:266:12:Times:12:Times:pascal_michaillat@brown.edu
2:52:3413:28:14:71:149:238:12:Times:12:Times:Emmanuel Saez
2:53:3426:14:14:71:197:224:12:Times:12:Times:Department of Economics
2:54:3449:14:14:71:236:210:12:Times:12:Times:University of California, Berkeley
2:55:3483:14:14:71:178:196:12:Times:12:Times:530 Evans Hall #3880
2:56:3503:14:14:71:170:182:12:Times:12:Times:Berkeley, CA 94720
2:57:3521:14:14:71:123:168:12:Times:12:Times:and NBER
2:58:3529:14:0:71:190:154:12:Times:12:Times:saez@econ.berkeley.edu
3:59:3551:0:34:254:357:701:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:1.  Introduction
3:60:3567:34:22:72:540:667:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:At the onset of the Great Recession governments responded to rising unemployment rates as they
3:61:3661:22:21:72:540:645:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:always  do:  by  lowering  interest  rates.   But  the  zero  lower  bound  on  the  nominal  interest  rate
3:62:3769:21:22:72:540:624:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:rapidly became an issue, prompting governments to look for alternative stabilization policies. One
3:63:3867:22:22:72:540:602:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:policy that had been used before and was considered again, was adjusting government purchases.
3:64:3961:22:21:72:540:580:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:However, as most modern research on stabilization had focused on monetary policy, policymakers
3:65:4055:21:22:72:365:559:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:had to base their decisions on fragmentary theoretical results.
3:66:4118:22:22:89:539:537:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In this paper we revisit and expand existing results on the optimal use of government purchases
3:67:4213:22:21:72:539:515:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:for stabilization.  The theoretical framework is a general-equilibrium matching model.1Govern-
3:68:4307:21:22:72:540:494:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ment purchases are valuable and financed by taxes that keep the government budget balanced. We
3:69:4401:22:22:72:540:472:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:formulate the optimal policy with three sufficient statistics:  (1) the unemployment gap, which is
3:70:4499:22:21:72:540:450:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the difference between the current unemployment rate and the efficient unemployment rate;  (2)
3:71:4593:21:22:72:540:429:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the unemployment multiplier, which measures the reduction in unemployment rate caused by an
3:72:4684:22:22:72:540:407:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:increase in public consumption; and (3) the elasticity of substitution between public and private
3:73:4781:22:21:72:431:385:12:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:consumption, which describes the value of additional public consumption.2
3:74:4854:21:22:89:539:364:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our  starting  point  is  the  standard  public-economics  result  that  when  productive  efficiency
3:75:4955:22:22:71:539:342:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:holds, public goods should be provided to the point where the marginal rate of substitution between
3:76:5054:22:21:71:540:320:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:public and private consumption equals the marginal rate of transformation (Samuelson 1954).3The
3:77:5149:21:22:71:494:299:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Samuelson formula remains valid in our model when the unemployment rate is efficient.
3:78:5234:22:22:89:539:277:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:However, when unemployment is inefficiently high, productive efficiency fails and the Samuel-
3:79:5327:22:21:71:539:255:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:son formula does not apply.   Macroeconomics offers a basic insight for these situations:  if the
3:80:5424:21:22:71:539:234:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:output multiplier (the effect on output of an increase in government purchases) is larger than one,
3:81:5523:22:22:71:539:212:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:government spending should increase.  The logic is simple.  With a multiplier above one, higher
3:82:5618:22:21:71:539:190:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:government spending leads not only to higher public consumption but also to higher private con-
3:83:5713:21:19:71:539:169:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:sumption, so it is desirable.  During the Great Recession, this logic lead to a spurt of empirical
3:84:5811:19:15:85:540:150:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:1For other papers using matching models to address optimal policy questions, see for instanceBoone and Boven-
3:85:5920:15:9:72:470:135:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:berg(2002),Hungerb ̈uhler and Lehmann(2009),Lehmann, Parmentier and Van Der Linden(2011).
3:86:6009:9:15:85:539:126:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:2For a description of the sufficient-statistics approach, seeChetty(2009). For other papers using the approach, see
3:87:6124:15:12:72:539:111:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:for instanceChetty(2006,2008),Hendren(2015),Farhi and Gabaix(2015),Stantcheva(2015),Werquin(2016), and
3:88:6226:12:9:72:190:99:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Jacquet and Lehmann(2016).
3:89:6252:9:0:85:502:90:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:3For a survey of the literature on the optimal provision of public goods, seeKreiner and Verdelin(2012).
4:90:6357:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:research to determine whether the output multiplier was above or below one.  But the logic is in-
4:91:6454:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:complete. If more public spending yields more public consumption and more private consumption,
4:92:6548:22:21:72:539:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:public spending should increase forevermore, or until the multiplier falls below one.4Assuming
4:93:6642:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that the multiplier becomes less than one at some point, a key question remains: now that there is
4:94:6740:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:a tradeoff between public and private consumption, what should the government do?  This is also
4:95:6835:22:21:72:340:599:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the question if the multiplier is below one to begin with.
4:96:6893:21:22:89:539:578:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To address this question,Mankiw and Weinzierl(2011) use a disequilibrium model. They find
4:97:6982:22:22:72:540:556:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that government purchases should be above the Samuelson level to completely fill the output gap.
4:98:7078:22:21:72:540:534:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:However, the disequilibrium model is special.  Its output multiplier is exactly one, so an increase
4:99:7177:21:22:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in government activity does not affect private activity. There is no crowding out of private activity
4:100:7278:22:22:72:540:491:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:by government spending when government spending rises and no shift of resources back to private
4:101:7373:22:21:72:540:469:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:activity when government spending falls. This property has strong implications. For example, the
4:102:7469:21:22:72:485:448:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:social value of public spending is irrelevant for the optimal level of stimulus spending.
4:103:7558:22:22:89:539:426:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Using a matching model allows us to analyze optimal government spending when unemploy-
4:104:7644:22:21:72:540:404:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ment is inefficiently high and there is an actual tradeoff between public and private consumption.
4:105:7742:21:22:72:540:383:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The tradeoff exists because public consumption crowds out private consumption.  When the gov-
4:106:7835:22:22:72:540:361:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ernment increases its purchases, it increases the length of the queues to purchase goods and services
4:107:7936:22:21:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and thus discourages household purchases, generating crowding out. The amount of crowding out
4:108:8029:21:22:72:344:318:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:may vary with the unemployment rate (Michaillat 2014).
4:109:8083:22:22:89:539:296:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We find that when the unemployment rate is inefficiently high or low, government purchases
4:110:8173:22:21:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:should deviate from the Samuelson level to partially fill the unemployment gap.   Hence,  when
4:111:8267:21:22:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the unemployment multiplier is positive—such that an increase in government purchases reduces
4:112:8360:22:22:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the unemployment rate—optimal public spending is above the Samuelson level whenever unem-
4:113:8449:22:22:72:540:209:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ployment is inefficiently high.   To understand the result,  imagine that public consumption is at
4:114:8547:22:21:72:540:187:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the Samuelson level, the unemployment multiplier is positive, and unemployment is inefficiently
4:115:8642:21:19:72:540:166:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:high.  Keeping total consumption constant, increasing public consumption by 1 unit reduces pri-
4:116:8737:19:15:85:539:147:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:4Robert Barro has made this point: “If the multiplier is greater than one, as is apparently assumed by Team Obama,
4:117:8851:15:12:72:540:132:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the process is even more wonderful. In this case, real GDP rises by more than the increase in government purchases.
4:118:8966:12:12:72:540:120:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Thus, in addition to the free airplane or bridge, we also have more goods and services left over to raise private consump-
4:119:9088:12:12:72:540:108:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:tion or investment. In this scenario, the added government spending is a good idea even if the bridge goes to nowhere,
4:120:9206:12:12:72:540:96:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:or if public employees are just filling useless holes.  Of course, if this mechanism is genuine, one might ask why the
4:121:9324:12:12:72:540:84:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:government should stop with only $1 trillion of added purchases.” See Robert J. Barro, “Government Spending Is No
4:122:9437:12:0:72:533:72:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Free Lunch”, Wall Street Journal, January 2009, available athttp://www.wsj.com/articles/SB123258618204604599.
5:123:9547:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:vate consumption by 1 unit.  At the Samuelson level, the marginal utilities of public and private
5:124:9644:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:consumption are equalized.  Hence, the increase in public consumption has no first-order effect
5:125:9739:22:21:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:on welfare so far.  Since the unemployment multiplier is positive, increasing public consumption
5:126:9835:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:lowers unemployment.  Since unemployment is inefficiently high, reducing unemployment raises
5:127:9927:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:total consumption.  Now the increase in public consumption has a positive effect on welfare: it is
5:128:10025:22:21:72:275:599:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:therefore optimal to raise public spending.
5:129:10068:21:22:89:539:578:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Next, we study how much of the unemployment gap should be filled, and how much stimulus
5:130:10155:22:22:72:540:556:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:spending—the deviation of government spending from the Samuelson level—is required to achieve
5:131:10248:22:21:72:174:534:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:this desired outcome.
5:132:10269:21:22:89:539:513:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:First, we examine how the optimal level of stimulus spending depends on the size of the unem-
5:133:10362:22:22:72:540:491:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ployment multiplier. Nakamura and Steinsson (2014, pp.787–788) consider this question in a New
5:134:10456:22:21:72:540:469:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Keynesian model. They obtain a formula that implicitly characterizes optimal government spend-
5:135:10550:21:22:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ing, and they infer that stimulus spending should be larger when the multiplier is larger. However,
5:136:10649:22:22:72:540:426:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:this bang-for-the-buck logic is incomplete because it omits the response of output to government
5:137:10745:22:21:72:540:404:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:spending in the implicit formula. To address this typical limitation of implicit formulas, we develop
5:138:10846:21:22:72:517:383:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:an explicit formula that describes optimal stimulus spending as a function of fixed quantities.
5:139:10941:22:22:89:539:361:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our explicit formula shows that the optimal level of stimulus spending is increasing in the
5:140:11032:22:21:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:multiplier for small multipliers, is maximized for a moderate multiplier, and is decreasing in the
5:141:11130:21:22:72:540:318:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:multiplier for large multipliers.  When the unemployment multiplier is small, the response of un-
5:142:11227:22:22:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:employment to public spending is small, so the bang-for-the-buck logic holds. However, when the
5:143:11322:22:21:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:multiplier becomes large, the response of unemployment to public spending becomes important
5:144:11413:21:22:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and the logic breaks down. As the multiplier becomes large, crowding out of private consumption
5:145:11508:22:22:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:by public consumption becomes small, and optimal stimulus spending fills the unemployment gap
5:146:11601:22:22:72:540:209:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:nearly entirely.  As less spending is required to fill the unemployment gap when the multiplier is
5:147:11699:22:21:72:435:187:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:larger, the optimal level of stimulus spending is decreasing in the multiplier.
5:148:11778:21:22:89:539:166:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Then, we examine how the optimal level of stimulus spending depends on the usefulness of ad-
5:149:11870:22:22:72:540:144:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ditional public spending. We find that both the optimal level of stimulus spending and the fraction
5:150:11969:22:21:72:540:122:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of the unemployment gap that should be filled are increasing in the elasticity of substitution be-
5:151:12067:21:22:72:540:101:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tween public and private consumption. There are two interesting limit cases. With a zero elasticity
5:152:12166:22:0:72:540:79:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of substitution—new public workers dig and fill holes—public consumption beyond the Samuel-
6:153:12258:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:son level is useless. Since public consumption crowds out private consumption, it is never optimal
6:154:12356:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:to provide public consumption beyond the Samuelson level.   With an infinite elasticity of sub-
6:155:12451:22:21:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:stitution, public and private consumption are interchangeable, so it is optimal to maximize total
6:156:12548:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:consumption, irrespective of its composition.  Accordingly, it is optimal to fill the unemployment
6:157:12646:22:22:72:148:621:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:gap completely.
6:158:12661:22:21:89:539:599:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Finally, we examine how taxation affects the results.  The results are initially derived with a
6:159:12756:21:22:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fixed labor supply, and thus nondistortionary taxes.  But a prevalent concern is that when govern-
6:160:12854:22:22:72:540:556:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ment purchases are financed by distortionary taxes, the output multiplier could be negative as a
6:161:12950:22:21:72:540:534:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:result of the fall in labor supply caused by tax distortions, thus overturning the benefits of stimu-
6:162:13051:21:22:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:lus spending in slumps.  In fact, empirical evidence for the United States suggests that the output
6:163:13150:22:22:72:540:491:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:multiplier is negative once tax distortions are taken into account (Barro and Redlick 2011).  We
6:164:13246:22:21:72:540:469:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:therefore introduce endogenous labor supply and distortionary taxation. We find that all the results
6:165:13346:21:22:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:carry over.  We also find that the unemployment multiplier equals the output multiplier net of the
6:166:13444:22:22:72:540:426:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:labor-supply response due to distortionary taxation.  Since the labor-supply response is negative,
6:167:13542:22:21:72:540:404:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the unemployment multiplier is larger than the output multiplier.  With a strong negative labor-
6:168:13638:21:22:72:540:383:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:supply response, a negative output multiplier can coexist with a positive unemployment multiplier.
6:169:13736:22:22:72:540:361:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Hence, we cannot use the sign of the output multiplier to infer the sign of the unemployment mul-
6:170:13833:22:21:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tiplier and determine whether stimulus spending is desirable in slumps.   In fact,  a reduction in
6:171:13931:21:22:72:540:318:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:labor supply leads to lower output but higher tightness and lower unemployment in the matching
6:172:14025:22:22:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:model (Michaillat and Saez 2015). Therefore, the unemployment multiplier is larger once tax dis-
6:173:14121:22:21:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tortions are taken into account. This implies that if stimulus spending is desirable in slumps under
6:174:14221:21:22:72:423:253:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:nondistortionary taxation, it is also desirable under distortionary taxation.
6:175:14298:22:22:89:539:231:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In this paper we limit ourselves to static considerations and skirt around dynamic considera-
6:176:14391:22:22:72:540:209:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tions.5However, to gain a more complete understanding of how public spending can be used for
6:177:14483:22:21:72:540:187:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:stabilization, it would be useful to enrich our static analysis with dynamic elements.  Several dy-
6:178:14582:21:22:72:540:166:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:namic elements seem important: the intertemporal smoothing of distortionary taxes and the use of
6:179:14678:22:18:72:540:144:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:debt, as in Barro (1979); the distinction between temporary and permanent changes in government
6:180:14773:18:16:85:539:126:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:5In the data the transitional dynamics of unemployment are extremely fast and inflation displays a large amount of
6:181:14887:16:12:72:540:110:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:inertia. Given these observations, we opt to abstract from the transitional dynamics of unemployment and from price
6:182:15002:12:12:72:540:98:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:dynamics. As a result, our dynamic model immediately converges to steady state from any initial condition. Thus, the
6:183:15118:12:0:72:323:86:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:analysis is essentially static even though the model is dynamic.
7:184:15183:0:22:72:539:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:spending, as in Barro(1981); the dynamic response of inflation to public spending, especially in
7:185:15279:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:a liquidity trap,  as inWoodford(2011) andWerning(2012);  government investment on infras-
7:186:15369:22:21:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tructure projects, as inBaxter and King(1993); and the political process leading to the design of
7:187:15466:21:45:72:326:643:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:stimulus packages, as inBattaglini and Coate(2016).
7:188:15517:45:34:105:507:598:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:2.  A Matching Model for the Analysis of Government Purchases
7:189:15578:34:22:72:540:564:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:This section presents the matching model used for the analysis of optimal government purchases.
7:190:15673:22:21:72:540:542:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The model is dynamic and set in continuous time. There are two goods: private services, purchased
7:191:15770:21:22:72:540:521:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:by households, and public services, purchased by the government. Government purchases are valu-
7:192:15865:22:22:72:540:499:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:able to households, as inSamuelson(1954). Government purchases contribute to macroeconomic
7:193:15955:22:21:72:313:477:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:stabilization by influencing the aggregate demand.
7:194:16005:21:22:89:539:456:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The supply structure of the model is borrowed fromMichaillat and Saez(2015).  Services are
7:195:16095:22:22:72:540:434:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:produced by self-employed households and traded on a matching market.  Not all the available
7:196:16187:22:21:72:540:412:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:services are sold at any point in time, so there is always some unemployment. Whereas the supply
7:197:16283:21:22:72:540:391:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:structure is specific,  the demand structure and price mechanism are generic.   FollowingChetty
7:198:16378:22:22:72:540:369:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(2006,2008),  we will express the formula with sufficient statistics that summarize the relevant
7:199:16474:22:43:72:334:347:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:features of the demand structure and price mechanism.
7:200:16527:43:30:72:228:304:14:g_d0_f5:14:g_d0_f5:2.1.    The Supply Structure
7:201:16555:30:21:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The economy consists of a government and a measure 1 of identical households.  Households are
7:202:16648:21:22:72:539:253:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:self-employed,  producing  and selling  services  on a  matching  market.6There  are two  types  of
7:203:16747:22:22:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:services:  private services and public services.  Public and private services are produced using the
7:204:16847:22:21:72:540:209:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:same technology.   The government purchases public services and households purchases private
7:205:16939:21:22:72:397:188:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:services. All services are sold on the same market at the same price.
7:206:17008:22:22:89:540:166:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Each household has a fixed productive capacityk; the productive capacity indicates the max-
7:207:17099:22:21:72:540:144:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:imum amount of services that a household could sell at any point in time.  Households sellC(t)
7:208:17193:21:19:72:540:123:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:services to other households andG(t)services to the government.  The output of services is the
7:209:17287:19:16:85:539:104:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:6We assume that households cannot consume their own labor services. For simplicity, we abstract from firms and
7:210:17397:16:12:72:539:88:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:assume that all production directly takes place within households.Michaillat and Saez(2015) show how the model
7:211:17507:12:0:72:531:76:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:can be modified to include firms hiring workers on a labor market and selling their production on a product market.
8:212:17623:0:40:72:341:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:sum of household purchases and government purchases:
8:213:17675:40:40:258:352:668:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f7:Y(t) =C(t)+G(t).
8:214:17691:40:21:72:496:628:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The matching process prevents households from selling their entire capacity soY(t)<k.
8:215:17776:21:22:89:540:607:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The services are sold through long-term relationships. The relationships separate at rates>0.
8:216:17869:22:22:72:540:585:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:SinceY(t)services are committed to existing relationships, households’ idle capacity isk−Y(t).
8:217:17963:22:21:72:515:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The unemployment rate is the share of households’ capacity that is idle:u(t) = (k−Y(t))/k.
8:218:18053:21:22:89:539:542:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To purchase labor services, households and government advertisev(t)vacancies.  The rate at
8:219:18143:22:40:72:519:520:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:which new long-term relationships are formed is given by a Cobb-Douglas matching function
8:220:18232:40:39:230:381:480:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f7:h(t) =ω·(k−Y(t))η·v(t)1−η,
8:221:18258:39:22:72:448:441:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:whereη∈(0,1)is the matching elasticity, andω>0 is the matching efficacy.
8:222:18330:22:22:89:539:419:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f8:The market tightnessx(t)is the ratio of the two arguments in the matching function:x(t)≡
8:223:18418:22:21:72:539:397:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:v(t)/(k−Y(t)).   With  constant  returns  to  scale  in  matching,  the  tightness  determines  the  rates
8:224:18524:21:22:72:540:376:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:at which sellers and buyers enter into new long-term trading relationships.  Each of thek−Y(t)
8:225:18618:22:22:72:540:354:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:units of idle capacity is sold at ratef(x(t)) =h(t)/(k−Y(t)) =ω·x(t)1−ηand each of thev(t)
8:226:18708:22:21:71:540:332:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:vacancies is filled at rateq(x(t)) =h(t)/v(t) =ω·x(t)−η.  The selling ratef(x)is increasing in
8:227:18802:21:22:71:540:311:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:xand the buying rateq(x)is decreasing inx.  Hence, when tightness is higher, it is easier to sell
8:228:18899:22:22:71:405:289:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:services but harder to buy them. A useful result is thatf(x) =q(x)·x.
8:229:18968:22:21:89:540:267:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Output is a state variable with law of motion ̇Y(t) =f(x(t))·(k−Y(t))−s·Y(t).  The term
8:230:19055:21:22:73:539:246:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:f(x(t))·(k−Y(t))is the number of new relationships formed at timet.  The terms·Y(t)is the
8:231:19144:22:22:71:540:224:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:number of existing relationships separated at timet.  Iff(x)andsare constant over time, output
8:232:19238:22:39:71:234:202:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:converges to the steady-state level
8:233:19273:39:0:71:298:163:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:(1)Y(x,k) =
8:234:19284:0:16:312:332:171:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f6:f(x)
8:235:19288:16:0:304:341:155:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:f(x)+s
8:236:19294:0:40:343:357:163:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f7:·k.
8:237:19297:40:21:72:540:123:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In practice, output reaches this steady-state level quickly because market flows are large. Through-
8:238:19397:21:22:72:540:102:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:out the paper, we therefore simplify the analysis by modeling output as a jump variable equal to
8:239:19493:22:0:72:539:80:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:its steady-state value defined by (1).  The functionY(x,k)is increasing inxandk[0,+∞), with
9:240:19585:0:22:71:539:708:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:Y(0,k) =0 and limx→+∞Y(x,k) =k. When tightness is higher, it is easier to sell services so output
9:241:19682:22:22:71:394:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is higher. The elasticity ofY(x,k)with respect toxis(1−η)·u(x).
9:242:19745:22:21:89:540:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The unemployment rate is directly related to output:u=1−Y/k.  Hence, the simplification
9:243:19832:21:40:71:317:643:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:also implies that the unemployment rate is given by
9:244:19883:40:0:71:299:603:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:(2)u(x) =
9:245:19892:0:16:319:324:611:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:s
9:246:19893:16:0:302:341:595:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f6:s+f(x)
9:247:19899:0:40:342:345:603:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:.
9:248:19900:40:21:71:540:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The functionu(x)is decreasing inx,  withu(0) =1 and limx→+∞u(x) =0.   When tightness is
9:249:19987:21:22:71:539:542:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:higher, it is easier to sell services so the unemployment rate is lower.  The elasticity ofu(x)with
9:250:20086:22:22:71:540:520:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:respect toxis−(1−η)·(1−u(x)). InAppendix A, we show that in US data, the unemployment
9:251:20171:22:21:71:413:498:12:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:rate given by (2) and the actual employment rate are indistinguishable.7
9:252:20243:21:22:89:539:477:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Advertising vacancies is costly. Posting one vacancy costsρ>0 services per unit time. Hence,
9:253:20335:22:22:71:539:455:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:a total ofρ·v(t)services are spent at timeton filling vacancies.  These services represent the re-
9:254:20433:22:21:71:539:433:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:sources devoted by households and government to matching with appropriate providers of services.
9:255:20529:21:22:71:539:412:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:These resources devoted to matching are not consumed by households in that they do not enter
9:256:20621:22:22:71:539:390:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:their utility function. Hence, households’ consumption of private services, denoted byc(t), equals
9:257:20719:22:21:71:539:368:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:household purchases net of the matching costs incurred by households, households’ consumption
9:258:20812:21:22:71:540:347:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of public services, denoted byg(t), equals government purchases net of the matching costs incurred
9:259:20910:22:22:71:540:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:by the government, and households’ total consumption of services, denoted byy(t) =c(t)+g(t),
9:260:21002:22:21:71:539:303:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:equals output net of total matching costs.  We refer toc(t)as private consumption,g(t)as public
9:261:21097:21:22:72:283:282:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:consumption, andy(t)as total consumption.
9:262:21138:22:22:89:540:260:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:Equation (1) and the definition of the market tightness imply thats·Y(t) =f(x(t))·(k−Y(t)) =
9:263:21230:22:21:72:539:238:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f6:q(x(t))·v(t).   Hence,y(t) =Y(t)−ρ·v(t) =Y(t)−ρ·s·Y(t)/q(x(t)).   Consequently,Y(t) =
9:264:21315:21:40:72:191:217:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:y(t)·[1+τ(x(t))], where
9:265:21338:40:0:71:291:177:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f8:(3)τ(x)≡
9:266:21346:0:16:312:331:185:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f5:ρ·s
9:267:21349:16:0:296:348:169:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:q(x)−ρ·s
9:268:21357:0:40:349:352:177:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:.
9:269:21358:40:21:71:540:137:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Hence, consuming one service requires to purchase 1+τservices—one service for consumption
9:270:21447:21:19:72:540:116:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:plusτservices for matching.  This logic implies that private consumption is related to household
9:271:21543:19:15:85:539:97:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:7We follow the approach ofHall(2005) andPissarides(2009), who simplify their analysis by ignoring the transi-
9:272:21652:15:0:72:499:82:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:tional dynamics of unemployment and assuming that unemployment is a function of tightness given by (2).
10:273:21756:0:22:72:539:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:purchases byc(t) =C(t)/[1+τ(x(t))]and public consumption to government purchases byg(t) =

10:276:22023:21:22:71:539:643:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is more difficult to match with a seller so the matching wedge is higher. The elasticity ofτ(x)with

10:278:22146:22:39:89:410:599:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We write total consumption as a function of tightness and capacity:
10:279:22213:39:0:71:297:560:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:(4)y(x,k) =

11:340:24107:171:26:329:519:531:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B.  Efficient and inefficient unemployment rates
11:341:24155:26:38:229:381:505:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figure 1: The Matching Market
11:342:24184:38:22:71:539:467:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:capacity is idle,  and a marginal decrease in unemployment increases total consumption.  When
11:343:24277:22:22:71:539:445:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:unemployment is inefficiently low, too many resources are devoted to purchasing labor services,
11:344:24372:22:21:71:539:423:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and a further decrease in unemployment reduces total consumption.  The efficient unemployment
11:345:24465:21:44:71:484:402:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:rateu∗is the unemployment rate underlying the efficiency condition of Hosios (1990).
11:346:24549:44:29:71:446:358:14:g_d0_f5:14:g_d0_f5:2.2.    The Demand Structure, Price Mechanism, and Equilibrium
11:347:24611:29:22:71:539:329:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In developing the demand structure of the model, we have two objectives. The first is to develop an
11:348:24710:22:22:71:539:307:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:aggregate demand rich enough to capture the different possible effects of government purchases,
11:349:24805:22:21:71:539:285:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:such as the stimulus of aggregate demand by government purchases or the crowding out of private
11:350:24900:21:22:71:248:264:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:consumption by public consumption.
11:351:24934:22:22:89:539:242:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:These effects are not necessarily present in macroeconomic models. Typical matching models
11:352:25024:22:21:71:539:220:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:are an example.  In these models,  a free-entry condition determines equilibrium tightness.  The
11:353:25120:21:22:71:539:199:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:free-entry condition is independent of government purchases so an increase in government pur-
11:354:25213:22:22:71:540:177:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:chases has no effect on tightness and total consumption. As discussed inMichaillat(2014), public
11:355:25309:22:21:71:539:155:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:consumption therefore crowds out private consumption one-for-one.  To allow for less-than-full
11:356:25403:21:22:71:539:134:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:crowding out, we allow the aggregate demand to be less than perfectly tightness elastic.  Typical
11:357:25500:22:22:71:539:112:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:disequilibrium models are another example: the demand for private consumption is unaffected by
11:358:25594:22:0:71:539:90:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:public consumption so there is no crowding out and the multiplier is exactly one (for example,
12:359:25690:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Mankiw and Weinzierl 2011).  The the multiplier also is exactly one in typical New Keynesian
12:360:25782:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:models when monetary policy is held constant (Woodford 2011). To allow for some crowding out,
12:361:25875:22:21:72:331:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:we allow the aggregate demand to be tightness elastic.
12:362:25929:21:22:89:539:643:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The advantage of a rich demand structure is to accommodate a wide range of multipliers. This
12:363:26021:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:facilitates the mapping between the model and the data. If the price of services does not respond to
12:364:26121:22:21:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:government purchases, utility is separable in private and public consumption, and taxation is lump
12:365:26219:21:22:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:sum, the output multiplier would be one in a disequilibrium model and zero in a matching model.
12:366:26314:22:22:72:540:556:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In our model, the output multiplier can be anywhere between zero and one because the aggregate
12:367:26408:22:21:72:441:534:12:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:demand is neither perfectly tightness inelastic nor perfectly tightness elastic.8
12:368:26489:21:22:89:539:513:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The second objective is to develop an aggregate demand that is nondegenerate such that aggre-
12:369:26582:22:22:72:540:491:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:gate demand and supply intersect to give the equilibrium level of tightness.  To avoid degeneracy,
12:370:26680:22:21:72:540:469:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the aggregate demand curve needs to involve the tightness and price of services. This requirement
12:371:26777:21:22:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:on the aggregate demand is equivalent to preventing the demand and supply curves of a Walrasian
12:372:26872:22:22:72:540:426:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:market to be both price inelastic.  Indeed, if both demand and supply are perfectly price inelastic
12:373:26971:22:21:72:540:404:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(vertical in a standard price-quantity diagram), the equilibrium exists only if the two curves overlap
12:374:27073:21:22:72:536:383:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and the intersection of the two curves does not determine a price. We want to avoid this problem.
12:375:27170:22:22:89:539:361:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To generate an aggregate demand satisfying the requirements, we introduce an asset in fixed
12:376:27261:22:21:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:supply and assume that households derive utility from holding this asset. Households spend part of
12:377:27359:21:22:72:540:318:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:their labor income on services and save part of it using the asset. Household hold the asset because
12:378:27459:22:39:72:507:296:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:they desire to smooth consumption over time and they derive utility from holding the asset.
12:379:27550:39:21:72:540:257:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:An  Example  with  Land.The  asset  that  we  introduce  is  land.   Households  derive  utility  from
12:380:27652:21:22:72:539:236:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:holdingl(t)units of land. This utility captures for instance the housing services provided by land.
12:381:27751:22:22:72:539:214:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Land is traded on a perfectly competitive market. The supply of land is fixed atl0. In equilibrium,
12:382:27850:22:21:71:539:192:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the land market clears sol(t) =l0. This demand structure is similar to the structure found in models
12:383:27950:21:22:71:539:171:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that study the role of land and land prices in causing or propagating business cycles. For instance,
12:384:28050:22:22:71:539:149:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:models by Iacoviello (2005), Liu, Wang and Zha (2013), and Kocherlakota (2013) assume that
12:385:28140:22:21:71:536:127:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:land enters the utility function, is traded on a perfectly competitive market, and is in fixed supply.
12:386:28242:21:19:89:539:106:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The price of services in terms of land isp(t). If the market for services was perfectly compet-
12:387:28337:19:15:85:539:87:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:8If the price of services responds to government purchases, utility is not separable, and taxation is distortionary,
12:388:28453:15:0:72:293:72:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the output multiplier can be negative or larger than one.
13:389:28512:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:itive, the price would be determined such that the supply and demand of services are equal.  On
13:390:28607:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:a matching market things are different; we specify a general price mechanism that determines the
13:391:28703:22:21:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:price of services:p(t) =p(g(t)).  Given the price of services, tightness adjusts such that supply
13:392:28800:21:22:72:273:643:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:equals demand on the market for services.
13:393:28841:22:22:89:539:621:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The government balances its budget at all times using a lump-sum taxT(t) =G(t)levied on
13:394:28928:22:21:72:129:599:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:households.
13:395:28939:21:22:89:539:578:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The household derives utility from consumingc(t)private services andg(t)public services,
13:396:29027:22:22:72:539:556:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:and from owningl(t)units of land. Its instantaneous utility function is separable:U(c(t),g(t))+

14:418:30234:22:22:89:539:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We now describe the equilibrium for a given public consumption,g.  An equilibrium consists

14:428:31184:22:21:71:539:469:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:source.  As there is no state variable, the system immediately jumps to the steady state from any
14:429:31281:21:22:71:150:448:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:initial condition.

14:445:32034:22:22:72:540:195:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:spending the same amount on private services.  The equation determines the aggregate demand,
14:446:32126:22:21:72:540:173:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:c(x,p,g)+g. Aggregate demand shocks are shocks to the marginal utility of land,V′(l0), or to the
14:447:32222:21:22:71:539:152:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:time discount rate,δ; with higher marginal utility of land or lower time discount rate, households
14:448:32320:22:0:71:427:130:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:desire to save more and consume less, which depresses aggregate demand.
15:449:32393:0:40:89:525:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The constraint that aggregate supplyy(x,k)equals aggregate demandc(x,p,g)+gimposes
15:450:32475:40:40:72:367:668:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f7:(11)y(x,k) =c(x,p(g),g)+g.
15:451:32501:40:38:72:529:628:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:This equation implicitly defines equilibrium tightness as a functionx(g)of public consumption.
15:452:32595:38:22:72:540:590:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:The Generic Case.InAppendix Bwe provide three other examples of demand structure and
15:453:32679:22:21:72:540:568:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:price mechanism:  one with an unproduced good,  one with money,  and one with bonds.  These
15:454:32770:21:22:72:420:547:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:three examples yield the same equilibrium structure as the land example.
15:455:32842:22:22:89:539:525:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In all the examples, the equilibrium immediately converges to steady state. In the steady-state
15:456:32937:22:21:72:540:503:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:equilibrium, tightness is a function of the provision of public services:x=x(g).  The tightness
15:457:33032:21:22:71:540:482:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:functionx(g)is determined by households’ utility function, the price mechanism, and the supply
15:458:33126:22:22:71:539:460:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:structure. It summarizes everything that the government needs to know about the demand structure
15:459:33222:22:21:71:540:438:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in the economy.  With knowledge of the tightness functionx(g)and the supply structure of the
15:460:33314:21:22:71:539:417:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:economy, the government will determine the optimal provision of public services.  The optimal
15:461:33407:22:22:71:540:395:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:gmaximizesU(c,g) =U(y(x(g),k)−g,g).   The  utility  over  the asset  does  not  enter welfare
15:462:33500:22:21:71:240:373:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:because the asset is in fixed supply.
15:463:33537:21:22:89:539:352:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In general on the matching market the price mechanism does not guarantee efficiency.  Since
15:464:33628:22:22:71:539:330:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:search  is  random,  prices  are  determined  in  a  situation  of  bilateral  monopoly,  and  there  are  no
15:465:33737:22:21:71:539:308:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:market forces ensuring that the price of services relative to the asset maintains the unemployment
15:466:33835:21:22:71:539:287:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:rate at its efficient level (Pissarides 2000, Chapter 8). Since prices do not ensure efficiency, policies
15:467:33940:22:22:71:513:265:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:are useful to stabilize the economy—that is, bring unemployment closer to its efficient level.
15:468:34034:22:21:89:539:243:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In our theory, we take as given all other potential policies that could affect economic activity.
15:469:34131:21:22:71:539:222:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:These other policies could fully stabilize the economy.  Our analysis would trivially apply in that
15:470:34230:22:22:71:539:200:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:case. But these policies may not be able to keep unemployment at its efficient level.9Our analysis
15:471:34328:22:21:71:539:178:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:concentrates on these cases. In our example with bonds, monetary policy could adjust the nominal
15:472:34424:21:22:71:539:157:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:interest rate to bring the economy to efficiency, but constraints such as the zero lower bound prevent
15:473:34526:22:18:71:539:135:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:monetary policy to achieve this goal perfectly.  In the other examples taxes could affect relative
15:474:34624:18:16:85:540:117:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:9We take the same approach asEggertsson and Woodford(2006) andFarhi and Werning(2016).  Eggertsson and
15:475:34726:16:12:71:539:101:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Woodford study optimal monetary policy taking fiscal policy as given and assuming that fiscal policy fails to eliminate
15:476:34845:12:12:71:539:89:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the decline in interest rate that led to a liquidity trap. Farhi and Werning study macroprudential policies assuming that
15:477:34966:12:0:71:499:77:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:monetary policy and tax instruments are unable to undo price rigidities and achieve the first-best allocation.
16:478:35078:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:prices and bring the economy closer to efficiency, but the taxes may be difficult to implement or
16:479:35175:22:45:72:438:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:have costs making it suboptimal to bring unemployment to its efficient level.
16:480:35252:45:34:163:447:641:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:3.  Optimal Government Purchases Formulas
16:481:35293:34:21:71:539:607:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:This section describes the optimal level of government purchases in the model of Section 2.  We
16:482:35388:21:22:71:539:586:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:obtain formulas that relate the optimal level of government purchases to the Samuelson level, the
16:483:35485:22:22:71:539:564:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:unemployment gap, the unemployment multiplier, and the elasticity of substitution between public
16:484:35581:22:21:71:192:542:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and private consumption.
16:485:35605:21:22:89:539:521:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The rest of the paper will complement this section in several ways.  Section 4shows that the
16:486:35697:22:22:71:539:499:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:formulas obtained here under exogenous labor supply remain the same under endogenous labor
16:487:35787:22:21:71:540:477:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:supply and distortionary taxation.  Section5 explains the relationship between the unemployment
16:488:35882:21:22:71:539:456:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:multiplier used in our formulas and the output multiplier commonly used in academic and policy
16:489:35976:22:22:71:540:434:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:discussions.  Section6 offers a numerical application to the Great Recession in the United States.
16:490:36074:22:21:71:539:412:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The application shows how to calibrate the formulas and provides orders of magnitude for the
16:491:36166:21:22:71:540:391:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:optimal policy response at the onset of Great Recession. Last, Section7 uses simulations to check
16:492:36263:22:44:71:459:369:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the accuracy of our formulas, which are derived using first-order approximations.

18:581:39853:22:21:71:539:599:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:as long as productive efficiency is satisfied.   The Samuelson formula was originally derived in
18:582:39949:21:22:71:539:578:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:a  neoclassical  model,  which  is  very  different  from  our  matching  model,  so  this  result  was  not
18:583:40057:22:22:71:539:556:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:completely obvious.   This result suggests that the Samuelson formula is robust:  it applies to a
18:584:40154:22:21:71:364:534:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:broad range of models as long as productive efficiency holds.
18:585:40215:21:22:89:539:513:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:An implication of the formula is that the provision of public services is sometimes justified
18:586:40308:22:22:71:539:491:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:even if public services are not as valuable as private services.  Imagine that one public service is
18:587:40408:22:21:71:539:469:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:never as valuable as one private service:∂U/∂g<∂U/∂corMRSgc<1 for any(c,g).  In that
18:588:40492:21:22:71:540:448:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:case the Samuelson formula indicates that no public services should be provided:g=0.  But in a
18:589:40586:22:22:71:539:426:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:matching model, it may be optimal to provide some public services for stabilization. This happens
18:590:40683:22:21:71:424:404:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:when the correction term evaluated atg=0 is greater than 1−MRSgc(0).

19:617:41785:40:21:89:540:628:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The Samuelson level is the level ofG/Cthat satisfies the Samuelson formula.  WhenG/Cis
19:618:41871:21:22:72:540:607:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:at the Samuelson level, the marginal values from public and private consumption are equal. Since
19:619:41967:22:22:72:540:585:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:MRSgc(0)≥1 andMRSgcis decreasing inG/C, the Samuelson level is always well defined.  The
19:620:42055:22:21:72:540:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Samuelson level is determined by households’ preferences,  so it does not depend on economic
19:621:42147:21:22:72:125:542:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:conditions.
19:622:42158:22:22:89:547:520:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The elasticity of substitution between public and private consumption measures how the marginal
19:623:42253:22:21:72:539:498:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:rate of substitution between public and private consumption varies withG/C. SinceMRSgcis de-
19:624:42345:21:22:72:540:477:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:creasing inG/C, the elasticity of substitution is positive. A lower elasticity of substitution implies
19:625:42447:22:22:72:540:455:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that the marginal value of public consumption, measured relative to the marginal value of private
19:626:42544:22:21:72:540:433:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:consumption, decreases faster withG/C.  The elasticity of substitution has two interesting limits.
19:627:42642:21:22:72:539:412:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Whenε→0, public and private consumption are perfect complement.13This means that a certain
19:628:42732:22:22:72:540:390:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:number of public services are needed for a given economy, but beyond that number, additional
19:629:42824:22:21:72:540:368:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:public services have zero value—additional public workers dig and fill holes.   In that case,  the
19:630:42922:21:22:72:540:347:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:marginal rate of substitution falls to zero as soon the required number of public services is pro-
19:631:43020:22:22:72:540:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:vided.  Whenε→+∞, the public and private consumption are perfect substitute.14This means
19:632:43108:22:21:72:540:303:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that households are equally happy to consume a unit of private or public services. In that case, the
19:633:43208:21:22:72:284:282:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:marginal rate of substitution is constant at 1.
19:634:43255:22:22:89:540:260:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The unemployment multiplier measures the percent increase in employment, 1−u, when pub-
19:635:43342:22:21:72:539:238:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f8:lic  consumption  increases  by  1  percent  of  total  consumption.   In  practice,  1−u≈1  som≈
19:636:43439:21:22:72:539:217:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:−du/(dg/y).  Hence, the unemployment multiplier approximately gives the decrease of the un-
19:637:43530:22:22:72:540:195:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:employment rate, measured in percentage points, when public consumption increases by 1 percent
19:638:43624:22:21:72:174:173:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of total consumption.
19:639:43645:21:22:89:539:152:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The Samuelson level and the elasticity of substitution reflect the value that society places on
19:640:43740:22:22:72:540:130:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:public services.  We will not estimate them, but treat them as an input for policy design.  On the
19:641:43838:22:18:72:540:108:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:other hand, we will obtain estimates of the unemployment multiplier from the empirical literature.
19:642:43936:18:12:82:376:90:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:13The Leontief utility functionU(c,g) =min{(1−γ)·c,γ·g}hasε=0.
19:643:43998:12:0:82:313:78:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:14The linear utility functionU(c,g) =c+ghasε→+∞.

21:763:46682:32:21:71:539:193:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:Proof.We obtain (19) by taking (12), approximating 1−MRSgcwith (16), approximating∂y/∂x
21:764:46769:21:31:71:269:172:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:with (17), and rewritingdx/dgwith (18).
21:765:46808:31:22:89:539:141:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Formula  (19)  relates  the  optimal  level  of  government  purchases  (G/C)  to  several  sufficient
21:766:46910:22:21:72:539:119:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:statistics:   the  matching  elasticity  (η),  the  unemployment  multiplier  (m),  the  Samuelson  level
21:767:47015:21:22:72:540:98:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:((G/C)∗), the elasticity of substitution between public and private consumption (ε), and the unem-
21:768:47113:22:0:72:539:76:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ployment gap (u−u∗).  The formula allows us to derive several qualitative properties of optimal
22:769:47210:0:22:72:182:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:government purchases.
22:770:47231:22:22:89:539:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The formula shows that the welfare-maximizing level of government purchases depends on
22:771:47317:22:21:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:a government-spending multiplier, confirming an intuition that macroeconomists have had for a
22:772:47410:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:long time. Academic and policy discussions about government spending, however, usually revolve
22:773:47504:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:around the output multiplier,  not the unemployment multiplier.   The output and unemployment
22:774:47597:22:21:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:multipliers are closely related, as we will show in Section 5.  But the unemployment multiplier
22:775:47692:21:22:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:has an advantage over the output multiplier: it remains a valid sufficient statistics when taxation is
22:776:47794:22:22:72:354:556:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:distortionary, which is not the case of the output multiplier.
22:777:47856:22:21:89:539:534:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:However,  the  multiplier  is  not  sufficient  to  measure  the  effect  of  government  purchases  on
22:778:47959:21:22:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:welfare because an increase in government purchases also affects the composition of households’
22:779:48054:22:22:72:540:491:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:consumption.  This is why of substitution between public and private consumption also enters the
22:780:48150:22:21:72:540:469:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:formula.  The elasticity matters because it determines how quickly the marginal value of public
22:781:48245:21:22:72:322:448:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:services fades when government purchases increase.
22:782:48295:22:22:89:539:426:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Formula (19) allows us to determine under which conditions public spending should be higher
22:783:48386:22:21:72:540:404:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:than the Samuelson level.  We find that when the unemployment multiplier is positive—such that
22:784:48480:21:22:72:540:383:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:an increase in government purchases reduces the unemployment rate—optimal public spending is
22:785:48572:22:22:72:540:361:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:above the Samuelson level whenever unemployment is inefficiently high. On the other hand, when
22:786:48666:22:21:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the unemployment multiplier is negative—such that an increase in government purchases raises
22:787:48758:21:22:72:540:318:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the unemployment rate—optimal public spending is above the Samuelson level whenever unem-
22:788:48847:22:22:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ployment is inefficiently low.  It is only if the unemployment multiplier is zero that government
22:789:48944:22:21:72:517:274:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:purchases should always be at the Samuelson level. These results are summarized in Table 1.
22:790:49035:21:22:89:539:253:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To understand these results, imagine that public consumption is at the Samuelson level, the
22:791:49126:22:22:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:unemployment multiplier is positive, and unemployment is inefficiently high.  Keeping total con-
22:792:49222:22:22:72:540:209:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:sumption  constant,  increasing  public  consumption  by  1  unit  reduces  private  consumption  by  1
22:793:49325:22:21:72:540:187:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:unit.  At the Samuelson level, the marginal utilities of public and private consumption are equal-
22:794:49423:21:22:72:540:166:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ized.  Hence, the increase in public consumption has no first-order effect on welfare so far.  Since
22:795:49523:22:22:72:540:144:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the unemployment multiplier is positive,  increasing public consumption lowers unemployment.
22:796:49615:22:21:72:540:122:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Since unemployment is inefficiently high, reducing unemployment raises total consumption. Once
22:797:49709:21:22:72:540:101:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the effect on government purchases on unemployment is accounted for, the increase in public con-
22:798:49805:22:0:72:540:79:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:sumption has a positive effect on welfare.  Thus, it is optimal to raise public spending above the
23:799:49905:0:21:92:519:701:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Table 1: The Optimal Level of Government Purchases Compared to the Samuelson Level

23:809:50344:22:22:89:539:508:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In fact, the sign of the unemployment multiplier determines the cyclicality of optimal govern-
23:810:50438:22:21:71:539:486:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ment purchases. Michaillat and Saez(2016) show that the unemployment gap is countercyclical in
23:811:50532:21:22:71:539:465:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:US data.  This empirical result, combined with our theoretical analysis, suggests that government
23:812:50629:22:22:71:539:443:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:purchases should be countercyclical if the unemployment multiplier is positive,  acyclical if the
23:813:50726:22:21:71:516:421:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:unemployment multiplier is zero, and procyclical if the unemployment multiplier is negative.
23:814:50818:21:22:89:539:400:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Formula (19) implies that the unemployment rate is inefficiently high or low, optimal govern-
23:815:50911:22:22:71:539:378:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ment purchases deviate from the Samuelson level to reduce the unemployment gap.   However,
23:816:51001:22:21:71:539:356:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:government purchases should fill the unemployment gap only partially, not completely. Indeed, if
23:817:51097:21:22:71:540:335:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the gap was completely filled by government spending, we would haveu=u∗butG/C6= (G/C)∗,
23:818:51184:22:22:71:539:313:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:which would violate the formula.  Overall, the formula shows that optimal government purchases
23:819:51278:22:43:71:459:291:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:depart from the Samuelson level to push unemployment toward its efficient level.
23:820:51358:43:30:71:223:248:14:g_d0_f5:14:g_d0_f5:3.2.    An Explicit Formula
23:821:51385:30:21:71:539:218:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Formula (19) characterizes the optimal level of government purchases implicitly.  Since the right-
23:822:51483:21:22:71:539:197:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f5:hand-side of the formula is endogenous to the policy, we cannot read the optimal level ofG/C
23:823:51575:22:22:71:539:175:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:off the formula. This means that we cannot use the formula to answer quantitative questions such
23:824:51671:22:21:71:539:153:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:as  “How  much  should  government  purchases  increase  if  the  unemployment  rate  rises  to  9%?”
23:825:51772:21:22:71:539:132:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and “How does the amplitude of the increase depend on the multiplier or the value of new public
23:826:51867:22:22:71:539:110:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:services?”.  This is a typical limitation of the sufficient-statistics approach, for which it has often
23:827:51970:22:0:71:539:88:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:been criticized (Chetty 2009).  Here we develop an explicit formula that addresses this limitation
24:828:52070:0:22:72:414:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and provides quantitative insights about optimal government purchases.
24:829:52140:22:22:89:540:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We assume that the unemployment rate is initially at an inefficient levelu06=u∗.  As govern-

28:1038:59733:30:31:71:328:656:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:Proof.The results directly follow from (20) and (21).
28:1039:59786:31:21:89:539:625:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:For concreteness the proposition considers positive unemployment multipliers and unemploy-
28:1040:59876:21:22:72:329:604:12:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:ment gaps, so optimal stimulus spending is positive.16
28:1041:59930:22:22:89:539:582:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The first part of the proposition studies how the optimal level of stimulus spending depends on
28:1042:60025:22:21:72:540:560:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the size of the unemployment multiplier. There is a presumption that stimulus spending should be
28:1043:60121:21:22:72:540:539:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:larger when the unemployment multiplier is larger.  At first glance, formula (19) seems to justify
28:1044:60219:22:22:72:539:517:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:this  bang-for-the-buck  logic:  for  a  givenu−u∗,  a  largermseems  to  indicate  that  the  optimal
28:1045:60321:22:21:72:539:495:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:G/C−(G/C)∗is larger.  In fact,Nakamura and Steinsson(2014, pp.787–788) derive a formula
28:1046:60408:21:22:72:540:474:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:similar to (19) in a new Keynesian model and conclude that “the extent of extra desirable spending
28:1047:60506:22:22:72:540:452:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:will depend on the size of the multiplier,  with a larger multiplier implying that more spending
28:1048:60602:22:21:72:540:430:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is desirable.”  However, this bang-for-the-buck logic is incomplete because it omits the response
28:1049:60699:21:22:72:540:409:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of unemployment to government spending in formula (19).  The multiplier also determines how
28:1050:60790:22:22:72:540:387:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:strongly unemployment responds to government purchases, and the link between the size of the
28:1051:60882:22:21:72:540:365:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:multiplier and the optimal level of stimulus spending is more complicated than suggested by the
28:1052:60977:21:22:72:188:344:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:bang-for-the-buck logic.
28:1053:61001:22:22:89:539:322:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The proposition shows that a higher unemployment multiplier does not necessarily entail a
28:1054:61090:22:21:72:540:300:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:stronger response of government purchases to fluctuations in unemployment. Instead, the optimal
28:1055:61185:21:22:72:540:279:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:level of stimulus spending for a given unemployment gap is a hump-shaped function of the unem-
28:1056:61279:22:22:72:540:257:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ployment multiplier:  the optimal level of stimulus spending is increasing in the multiplier until a
28:1057:61379:22:21:72:540:235:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:threshold, and decreasing in the multiplier after that. The multiplier that calls for the highest level
28:1058:61482:21:22:72:540:214:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of stimulus spending is given by (27).  The highest level of stimulus spending a given unemploy-
28:1059:61578:22:22:72:540:192:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ment gap is given by (28). We infer that the bang-for-the-buck logic applies when the multiplier is
28:1060:61677:22:21:72:328:170:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:below (27), but not when the multiplier is above (27).
28:1061:61731:21:22:89:539:149:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:There is a simple intuition behind this result. First, consider a small multiplier. We can neglect
28:1062:61829:22:22:72:540:127:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the feedback of government spending on unemployment because the multiplier is small. So in (19)
28:1063:61924:22:18:72:540:105:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:we can setu=u0, and it becomes clear thatG/Cincreases with the multiplier. Intuitively, for small
28:1064:62021:18:15:82:539:87:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:16We consider a positive unemployment multiplier because this case is the most empirically relevant, as discussed
28:1065:62134:15:0:72:417:72:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:in Section 6. We could derive similar results with a negative unemployment multiplier.
29:1066:62222:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:multipliers, the optimal level of government purchases is determined by the level of crowding out of
29:1067:62322:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:private consumption by public consumption. A higher multiplier means that there is less crowding
29:1068:62418:22:21:72:356:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:out and thus that government purchases are more desirable.
29:1069:62476:21:22:89:539:643:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Next,  consider a large multiplier.  Government purchases is such a potent policy that it can
29:1070:62569:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:close the unemployment gap without distorting much the allocation of output between public and
29:1071:62663:22:21:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:private consumption.  Hence, the optimal policy broadly is to fill the unemployment gapu0−u∗.
29:1072:62756:21:22:71:539:578:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In fact, unemployment under the optimal policy converges to efficient as the multiplier becomes
29:1073:62851:22:22:71:539:556:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:large, indicating that the unemployment gap is converging to zero. As the unemployment multiplier
29:1074:62948:22:21:71:539:534:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:rises, fewer government purchases are required to fill this unemployment gap, so the optimal level
29:1075:63046:21:22:71:314:513:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of stimulus spending decreases with the multiplier.
29:1076:63097:22:22:89:539:491:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The proposition also shows that a higher elasticity of substitution between public and private
29:1077:63191:22:21:71:539:469:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:consumption entails a stronger response of government purchases to fluctuations in unemployment.
29:1078:63287:21:22:71:539:448:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Both the optimal level of stimulus spending and the share of the unemployment gap filled under
29:1079:63381:22:22:71:378:426:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the optimal policy are increasing in the elasticity of substitution.
29:1080:63449:22:21:89:539:404:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:There  are  two  interesting  special  cases.   The  first  special  case  isε→0.   In  this  situation,
29:1081:63553:21:22:71:539:383:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:additional public services have zero value, so additional public workers dig and fill holes.  In that
29:1082:63654:22:22:71:539:361:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:case, the optimal stimulus spending is zero, irrespective of the unemployment rate and multiplier.
29:1083:63752:22:21:71:539:339:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Intuitively, public consumption beyond the Samuelson level is useless. Since public consumption
29:1084:63847:21:22:71:539:318:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:always crowds out private consumption, it is never optimal to provide more public consumption
29:1085:63940:22:22:71:221:296:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:than in the Samuelson formula.
29:1086:63970:22:21:89:540:274:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The second special case isε→+∞. In this situation, the public services provided by the gov-
29:1087:64061:21:22:71:539:253:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ernment perfectly substitute for the private services purchased by households. In that case, optimal
29:1088:64161:22:22:71:539:231:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:stimulus spending completely fills the unemployment gap such thatu=u∗. This result holds even
29:1089:64254:22:22:71:539:209:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:if the multiplier is very small and government purchases severely crowd out household purchases.
29:1090:64350:22:21:71:539:187:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Intuitively, public and private consumption are interchangeable, so it is optimal to maximize to-
29:1091:64447:21:22:71:539:166:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tal consumption, irrespective of its composition.  Accordingly, it is optimal to completely fill the
29:1092:64547:22:22:71:166:144:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:unemployment gap.
29:1093:64564:22:21:89:540:122:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f10:The result that government purchases should be used to fill the unemployment gap whenε→∞
29:1094:64652:21:22:71:539:101:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is reminiscent of the Keynesian result that government purchases should be used to fill the output
29:1095:64750:22:0:71:539:79:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:gap.   Mankiw and Weinzierl(2011) formally derive the Keynesian result with a disequilibrium
30:1096:64844:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:model. In their model, there is no crowding out of household purchases by government purchases.
30:1097:64939:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:If government purchases have some value,  government purchases should be increased until the
30:1098:65031:22:21:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f10:output gap is entirely filled. But the logics behind the Keynesian result and our result whenε→∞
30:1099:65127:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:are completely different.  The Keynesian result arises because there is no crowding out of private
30:1100:65225:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:consumption by public consumption.  In our model there is crowding out, but the composition of
30:1101:65319:22:21:72:496:599:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:total consumption does not matter whenε→∞, so the crowding out has no welfare cost.
30:1102:65402:21:22:89:539:578:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In reality, it is likely that public services have some value at the margin without being perfect
30:1103:65499:22:22:72:540:556:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:substitutes for private services; that is,ε>0 butε<+∞. In that case the optimal level of stimulus
30:1104:65596:22:21:72:540:534:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:spending  is  positive,  but  not  sufficient  to  completely  fill  the  unemployment  gap.   Hence,  even
30:1105:65703:21:22:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:with optimal government purchases, the unemployment rate remains inefficient. This result arises
30:1106:65799:22:45:72:344:491:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:because government purchases are not a first-best policy.
30:1107:65856:45:34:96:515:446:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:4.  Government Purchases Financed by a Distortionary Income Tax
30:1108:65919:34:21:72:540:412:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:So far we have abstracted from tax distortions. In this section we extend the model by introducing
30:1109:66017:21:22:72:540:391:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:an endogenous labor supply and a distortionary income tax. In this extended model, an increase in
30:1110:66114:22:22:72:540:369:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:government purchases affects the aggregate demand, as before, and the aggregate supply, because
30:1111:66209:22:21:72:395:347:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:it triggers an increase in taxes that affects households’ labor supply.
30:1112:66280:21:22:89:539:326:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We consider two types of taxes: a linear income tax, and a nonlinear income tax implemented
30:1113:66371:22:22:72:540:304:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:following the benefit principle. Using a linear income tax is the traditional approach in public eco-
30:1114:66472:22:21:72:540:282:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:nomics and the standard approach in macroeconomics.  Using the benefit principle is the modern
30:1115:66566:21:44:72:479:261:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:approach in public economics. In both cases, the results from Section 3 remain valid.
30:1116:66651:44:29:72:325:217:14:g_d0_f5:14:g_d0_f5:4.1.    The Traditional Approach to Taxation
30:1117:66695:29:22:72:539:188:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The representative household supplies a productive capacityk(t)at some utility cost. The choice of
30:1118:66793:22:22:72:539:166:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f8:k(t)is akin to a labor-supply decision. The instantaneous utility function becomesU(c(t),g(t))−
30:1119:66888:22:21:72:539:144:12:g_d0_f25:12:g_d0_f4:W(k(t)) +V(b(t)), where the functionWis strictly increasing inkand convex.  Since timing is
30:1120:66979:21:22:72:389:123:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:not ambiguous, we simplify notation by dropping the time indext.
30:1121:67043:22:22:89:539:101:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In this subsection, the government uses a linear income tax at rateτLto finance government
30:1122:67133:22:0:72:540:79:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:purchases. The household’s labor income becomes(1−τL)·Y(x,k) = (1−τL)·(1−u(x))·k. To
31:1123:67219:0:22:72:399:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:finance public consumptiong, the tax rate must beτL=G/Y=g/y.
31:1124:67279:22:22:89:540:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The  household  chooseskto  maximize  utility.   For  all  the  demand  structures  considered  in
31:1125:67377:22:39:72:410:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Section2 andAppendix B, the first-order condition with respect tokis
31:1126:67445:39:40:227:384:625:12:g_d0_f25:12:g_d0_f7:W′(k) =λ·(1−τL)·(1−u(x)),
31:1127:67470:40:22:71:540:585:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:whereλis the costate variable associated with real wealth in the household’s Hamiltonian.  We
31:1128:67563:22:39:71:519:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:combine this equation with the first-order condition with respect toc, given by (8). We obtain
31:1129:67657:39:0:71:328:524:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f8:(29)MRSkc= (1−τL)·
31:1130:67675:0:16:331:370:532:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:1−u(x)
31:1131:67681:16:0:331:371:516:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:1+τ(x)
31:1132:67687:0:40:371:374:524:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:,
31:1133:67688:40:22:71:539:484:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:whereMRSkc≡(∂W/∂k)/(∂U/∂c)is the marginal rate of substitution between labor and private
31:1134:67776:22:21:72:540:462:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:consumption. This equation describes households’ optimal labor supply. It says that the marginal
31:1135:67872:21:22:72:540:441:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:rate  of  substitution  between  labor  and  consumption  has  to  be  equal  to  the  post-tax  real  wage.
31:1136:67980:22:22:72:540:419:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:Indeed, one unit of labor is only sold with probability 1−u. When it is sold, it only yields 1/(1+τ)
31:1137:68080:22:21:72:539:397:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:units of consumption. Hence, the effective real wage is(1−u)/(1+τ)and the post-tax real wage
31:1138:68172:21:22:72:206:376:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is(1−τL)·(1−u)/(1+τ).
31:1139:68193:22:22:89:539:354:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The supply decision is distorted by the income tax: a higherτLimplies a lowerk. In fact, equa-
31:1140:68287:22:21:72:540:332:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tion (29) implicitly defines a functionk(g)that describes how the aggregate productive capacity
31:1141:68382:21:22:72:540:311:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:responds to a change in government purchases and the associated change in the income tax rate.
31:1142:68476:22:22:72:422:289:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Since the income tax is distortionary, the functionk(g)is decreasing ing.
31:1143:68549:22:21:89:539:267:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The welfare of an equilibrium isU(c,g)−W(k). Given a tightness functionx(g)and a capac-
31:1144:68636:21:22:72:539:246:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ity functionk(g), the government choosesgto maximizeU(y(x(g),k(g))−g,g)−W(k(g)). The
31:1145:68720:22:39:72:320:224:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:first-order condition of the government’s problem is

32:1211:69394:22:21:71:539:514:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ture once the Samuelson formula is modified to account for distortionary taxation.17Our optimal

32:1216:69865:22:22:72:540:406:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the marginal cost of funds is greater than one,  the modified Samuelson formula recommends a
32:1217:69957:22:21:72:540:384:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:lower level of government purchases than the regular formula.  Although the Samuelson level of
32:1218:70051:21:22:72:540:363:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:government purchases is lower with a linear income tax, the correction to the Samuelson formula
32:1219:70146:22:22:72:540:341:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is the same, so the deviation of optimal government purchases from the Samuelson level remains
32:1220:70240:22:31:72:465:319:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the same. In fact, the implicit formula (19) remains valid with a linear income tax:

32:1228:70825:20:15:82:540:118:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:17The modified Samuelson formula was developed byStiglitz and Dasgupta(1971) andAtkinson and Stern(1974)
32:1229:70929:15:12:72:540:103:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:to describe the optimal provision of public goods with a linear income tax.  A large literature has built on these two

33:1233:71296:22:31:72:376:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and (18) remain valid. Combining these results, we obtain (19).
33:1234:71359:31:21:89:539:655:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The unemployment multiplier in formula (19) is a policy elasticity, in the sense ofHendren
33:1235:71449:21:22:71:539:634:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(2015). It measures the change in unemployment for a change in government purchases accompa-
33:1236:71541:22:22:71:539:612:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:nied by the change in taxes maintaining a balanced government budget. In Section3 taxes are not
33:1237:71636:22:21:71:539:590:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:distortionary, so the unemployment multiplier should be measured using a policy reform in which
33:1238:71731:21:22:71:539:569:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:taxes are nondistortionary.  Here taxes are distortionary, so the unemployment multiplier should
33:1239:71827:22:22:71:539:547:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:be measured using a policy reform in which the tax change distorts the labor supply.  Moreover,
33:1240:71922:22:21:71:540:525:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Michaillat and Saez(2015) show that tightness rises and the unemployment rate falls in response
33:1241:72017:21:22:71:539:504:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:to a reduction in labor supply. Therefore, we expect unemployment multipliers to be larger under
33:1242:72113:22:22:71:354:482:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:distortionary taxation than under nondistortionary taxation.
33:1243:72173:22:31:89:422:460:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The explicit formula (20) also remains valid with a linear income tax:
