34:1283:73205:0:30:72:306:701:14:g_d0_f5:14:g_d0_f5:4.2.    The Modern Approach to Taxation
34:1284:73244:30:21:72:540:671:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:With homogenous households and endogenous labor supply, the government should raise revenue
34:1285:73335:21:22:72:540:650:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:with a lump-sum tax to avoid distortions.  In fact, with endogenous labor supply and a lump-sum
34:1286:73430:22:22:72:500:628:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tax, all the results obtained with exogenous labor supply in Section 3 would remain valid.
34:1287:73520:22:21:89:539:606:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:With heterogenous households, on the other hand, a distortionary tax system can be justified. It
34:1288:73616:21:22:72:540:585:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is justified if the government values redistribution (Diamond and Mirrlees 1971). It is also justified
34:1289:73718:22:22:72:540:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:if low-income workers are unable to pay a uniform lump-sum tax. These two reasons explain why
34:1290:73811:22:21:72:232:541:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:real tax systems are distortionary.
34:1291:73846:21:22:89:539:520:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To improve the realism of the analysis of Section3, we now assume that labor supply is en-
34:1292:73936:22:22:72:540:498:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:dogenous and government purchases are financed by a distortionary income tax. However, because
34:1293:74030:22:21:72:540:476:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:households are homogenous in the model, our welfare analysis cannot capture the benefits of the
34:1294:74125:21:22:72:540:455:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:distortionary income tax, such as higher redistribution. Our welfare analysis can only includes the
34:1295:74224:22:22:72:540:433:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cost of the distortionary income tax: a deadweight loss proportional to the labor-supply response.
34:1296:74322:22:21:72:540:411:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Because it considers the cost but not the benefits of the distortionary income tax, our welfare anal-
34:1297:74423:21:22:72:198:390:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ysis is bound to be biased.
34:1298:74450:22:22:89:539:368:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To overcome this bias, we follow the modern approach to taxation developed in public eco-
34:1299:74539:22:21:72:540:346:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:nomics.  This approach consists in using a nonlinear income tax scheduleT(k)and implementing
34:1300:74631:21:22:72:540:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tax reforms following the benefit principle.  With the income tax, the household’s disposable in-
34:1301:74728:22:22:72:539:303:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:come becomes(1−u(x))·(k−T(k)). Because the tax distortions exist for reasons unrelated to the
34:1302:74821:22:21:72:540:281:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:provision of public goods, the benefit principle argues that an increase in government purchases
34:1303:74917:21:22:72:539:260:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:should be financed by a tax increase that does not alter labor-supply distortions.18More precisely,
34:1304:75016:22:22:72:540:238:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:a change in government purchases is financed by a tax change designed to leave individual utility
34:1305:75113:22:21:72:540:216:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:unchanged for any level of labor supply. As a consequence, the labor-supply decision is unaffected
34:1306:75211:21:22:72:540:195:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:by the policy reform. Then, a Pareto improvement is possible if the reform generates a government
34:1307:75308:22:22:72:540:173:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:budget surplus or deficit. A surplus can be redistributed to households, creating a Pareto improve-
34:1308:75407:22:21:72:540:151:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ment. With a deficit, the opposite of the reform generates a surplus, making a Pareto improvement
34:1309:75504:21:19:72:540:130:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:possible. Hence, the formula for optimal government purchases ensures that any reform leaves the
34:1310:75600:19:15:82:540:111:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:18The benefit principle was introduced byHylland and Zeckhauser(1979) and generalized byKaplow(1996,1998).
34:1311:75706:15:12:71:539:96:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:For surveys of the modern approach to taxation, seeKaplow(2004) andKreiner and Verdelin(2012).  The modern
34:1312:75812:12:12:71:539:84:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:approach is closely related to the approach ofChristiansen(1981),Sandmo(1998),Coate(2000),Jacobs(2016), and
34:1313:75919:12:0:71:510:72:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:others, who study the optimal provision of public goods when taxes optimally satisfy redistributive objectives.
35:1314:76032:0:32:72:408:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:government budget balanced. We find that formula (12) does just that:
35:1315:76101:32:32:72:503:676:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:PROPOSITION8.In the model of Section 4.2, optimal government purchases satisfy(12).

36:1370:78403:45:33:84:527:434:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:5.  The Link Between Unemployment Multiplier and Output Multiplier
36:1371:78469:33:22:71:539:401:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The results in Sections3 and4 are based on the unemployment multiplier. But academic and policy
36:1372:78564:22:21:71:539:379:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:discussions about government spending usually involve the output multiplier.  In this section, we
36:1373:78661:21:22:71:539:358:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:explain how the unemployment and output multipliers are related, and we recast the results in terms
36:1374:78760:22:22:71:539:336:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of the output multiplier. We find that the unemployment multiplier equals the output multiplier net
36:1375:78859:22:21:71:539:314:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of supply-side responses.   Hence,  when taxation is nondistortionary,  unemployment and output
36:1376:78954:21:22:71:539:293:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:multipliers are the same, but when taxation is distortionary, they are substantially different and can
36:1377:79056:22:22:71:205:271:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:even have the opposite sign.
36:1378:79084:22:21:89:539:249:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:First, we introduce the empirical unemployment multiplier.  This multiplier will be a bridge
36:1379:79176:21:32:71:539:228:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:between the theoretical unemployment multiplier that enters our formulas and the output multiplier.

38:1517:82337:22:22:71:539:292:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:change in labor supply when government purchases increase by 1 percent of GDP. As the linear
38:1518:82429:22:21:71:539:270:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:income tax is distortionary, the supply-side response is negative and the unemployment multiplier
38:1519:82526:21:22:71:237:249:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is larger than the output multiplier.
38:1520:82563:22:22:89:539:227:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The unemployment multiplier is the correct sufficient statistic whether labor supply is exoge-
38:1521:82657:22:21:71:539:205:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:nous or endogenous, and whether taxation is distortionary or not.  With exogenous labor supply
38:1522:82751:21:22:71:539:184:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:or under the benefit principle, output and unemployment multipliers are the same so the output
38:1523:82845:22:22:71:539:162:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:multiplier matters for optimal government purchases exactly in the same way as the unemploy-
38:1524:82937:22:21:71:539:140:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ment multiplier.  With distortionary taxation, things are different.  Optimal government purchases
38:1525:83035:21:22:71:539:119:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:depend on the unemployment multiplier, and the unemployment multiplier is equal to the output
38:1526:83128:22:22:71:539:97:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:multiplier net of supply-side responses, so the output multiplier cannot be used directly to design
38:1527:83227:22:0:71:220:75:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:optimal government purchases.
39:1528:83258:0:22:89:539:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Empirical evidence hints that unemployment multiplier and output multiplier may not have the
39:1529:83350:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:same sign in the United States.Barro and Redlick(2011) find that the output multiplier is negative
39:1530:83448:22:21:72:539:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(around−0.6) once tax distortions are taken into account.  On the other hand,Monacelli, Perotti
39:1531:83543:21:22:72:539:643:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and Trigari(2010) andRamey(2013) finds that the empirical unemployment multiplier is positive
39:1532:83636:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(around 0.5). One potential issue is that the unemployment multipliers are estimated using deficit-
39:1533:83735:22:21:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:financed increases in government purchases,  not balanced-budget increases (Barro and Redlick
39:1534:83828:21:22:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:2011).  This issue is not very important here because unemployment multipliers are larger once
39:1535:83922:22:22:72:540:556:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the negative response of labor supply to distortionary taxes is taken into account.  This is because
39:1536:84022:22:21:72:540:534:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:a reduction in labor supply leads to higher tightness and lower unemployment in the matching
39:1537:84114:21:22:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:model (Michaillat and Saez 2015). Hence, 0.5 is a lower bound for the balanced-budget empirical
39:1538:84209:22:22:72:196:491:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:unemployment multiplier.
39:1539:84233:22:21:89:539:469:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Theory also shows that unemployment multiplier and output multiplier may have the opposite
39:1540:84323:21:22:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:sign.  In the matching model,  the unemployment multiplier is necessarily positive,  whereas the
39:1541:84419:22:22:72:448:426:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:output multiplier can be negative if labor-supply distortions are strong enough.
39:1542:84499:22:21:89:539:404:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:When the output multiplier is negative and the unemployment multiplier is positive, govern-
39:1543:84590:21:22:72:540:383:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ment purchases and the taxes used to finance them should be above the Samuelson level in slumps.
39:1544:84686:22:22:72:540:361:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:This is surprising. How can lowering output through higher taxes be optimal when output is already
39:1545:84784:22:21:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:inefficiently low? To understand this result, imagine that government purchases are the Samuelson
39:1546:84881:21:22:72:540:318:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:level and that unemployment is inefficiently high.  A small increase in government purchases re-
39:1547:84977:22:22:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:duces unemployment, reduces labor supply, and increase public consumption, which are all good
39:1548:85070:22:21:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:for welfare; but it reduces output and thus private consumption, which is bad for welfare.  At the
39:1549:85168:21:22:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Samuelson level, the cost of lower private consumption offsets the benefit of higher public con-
39:1550:85264:22:22:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:sumption and lower labor supply; the only remaining effect on welfare is the positive effect from
39:1551:85361:22:22:72:540:209:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:lower unemployment. (When the unemployment rate is efficient, variations in unemployment have
39:1552:85454:22:21:72:540:187:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:no first-order effects on welfare so the Samuelson level is optimal.) Overall, the small increase in
39:1553:85554:21:22:72:540:166:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:government purchases raises welfare.  Hence, it is optimal to raise government purchases above
39:1554:85648:22:22:72:540:144:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the Samuelson level.   At the same time,  the increase in government spending and taxes lowers
39:1555:85742:22:21:72:540:122:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:output because the reduction in output due to lower labor supply dominates the increase in output
39:1556:85839:21:22:72:540:101:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:due to lower unemployment.  But, because the reduction in output due to lower labor supply is
39:1557:85932:22:0:72:540:79:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:already internalized in the modified Samuelson formula, it is the increase in output due to lower
40:1558:86031:0:45:72:473:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:unemployment that determines the deviation from the modified Samuelson formula.
40:1559:86110:45:34:87:525:663:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:6.  A Numerical Application: The Great Recession in the United States
40:1560:86179:34:22:72:540:629:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In this section we use our explicit formula, given by (20), to compute the optimal response of gov-
40:1561:86278:22:21:72:540:607:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ernment purchases to the increase in unemployment observed at the onset of the Great Recession
40:1562:86372:21:22:72:540:586:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in the United States. We examine how the optimal policy response varies with the unemployment
40:1563:86465:22:22:72:540:564:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:multiplier and the elasticity of substitution between public and private consumption.  The results
40:1564:86563:22:21:72:194:542:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:are displayed in Figure 2.
40:1565:86589:21:22:89:539:521:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The starting point of the numerical application is 2008:Q3 in the United States.   Then,  the
40:1566:86682:22:22:72:539:499:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:unemployment rate wasu=6% and government purchases wereG/C=19.7%.19To simplify
40:1567:86760:22:21:72:539:477:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the analysis, we consider the unemployment rate in 2008:Q3 as efficient:u∗=6%.  This choice
40:1568:86851:21:22:72:540:456:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is reasonable as the unemployment rate in 2008:Q3 is close to its 25-year average, and there is
40:1569:86946:22:22:72:539:434:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:a presumption, going back at least toOkun(1963), that the economy is efficient on average.  If
40:1570:87040:22:21:72:540:412:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:unemployment is efficient in 2008:Q3, it is optimal for the government to follow the Samuelson
40:1571:87134:21:22:72:540:391:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:formula. To simplify the analysis further, we therefore set the Samuelson level to the government
40:1572:87231:22:22:72:540:369:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:purchases in 2008:Q3:(G/C)∗=19.7%.  This choice seems reasonable asG/Cin 2008:Q3 is
40:1573:87314:22:21:72:203:347:12:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:equal its 25-year average.20
40:1574:87342:21:22:89:539:326:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In 2008, a shock hit the US economy and unemployment started rising toward an inefficient
40:1575:87431:22:22:72:539:304:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:levelu0>u∗. In our model unemployment immediately reaches the higher levelu0, but in reality
40:1576:87523:22:21:72:540:282:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:unemployment slowly rises tou0.   The challenge for policymakers is to forecastu0before that
40:1577:87615:21:22:72:540:261:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:level is reached. In the winter 2008–2009, when the US government was designing their stimulus
40:1578:87709:22:22:72:539:239:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:package, they forecastedu0=9% (Romer and Bernstein 2009, Figure 1).  We therefore useu0=
40:1579:87797:22:21:72:232:217:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:9% for the numerical application.
40:1580:87830:21:22:89:539:196:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To apply formula (20), we need estimates of three statistics:  the elasticity of substitution be-
40:1581:87927:22:22:72:540:174:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tween  public  and  private  consumption  (ε),  the  matching  elasticity  (η),  and  the  unemployment
40:1582:88030:22:18:71:540:152:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:multiplier atu0(m0). First, the elasticityεreflect the value that society places on public services.
40:1583:88130:18:16:82:539:134:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:19We measureuas the quarterly average of the seasonally adjusted monthly unemployment rate constructed by
40:1584:88235:16:11:72:539:118:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:the Bureau of Labor Statistics (BLS) from the Current Population survey (CPS). To constructG/C, we measureG
40:1585:88342:11:12:72:540:107:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:as employment in the government industry andCas employment in the private industry.  BothGandCare quarterly
40:1586:88449:12:9:71:539:95:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:averages of seasonally adjusted monthly series constructed by the BLS from the Current Employment Statistics survey.
40:1587:88565:9:0:82:498:86:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:20Over the 1990–2014 period, the average unemployment rate is 6.1% and the average ofG/Cis 19.7%.
41:1588:88664:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:It is an input into the design of the optimal policy,  so we consider several values that span the
41:1589:88762:22:22:72:539:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:range of possibilities:ε=0.5,ε=1, andε=2.21Second, Landais, Michaillat and Saez (2015)
41:1590:88848:22:21:72:539:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:review the literature estimating matching functions on labor market data, and pickη=0.6 as their
41:1591:88944:21:22:72:322:643:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:preferred estimate. We follow them and setη=0.6.
41:1592:88992:22:22:89:539:621:12:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:Last, we determine a plausible range for the multiplierm0. Since the theoretical multiplierm0
41:1593:89085:22:21:71:539:599:12:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:is difficult to observe, we report estimates of the empirical multiplierM0.22We then translateM0
41:1594:89181:21:22:71:540:578:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:intom0using (33).  In fact, as above, we can set(G/Y)∗=0.197/(1+0.197) =16.5%,η=0.6,
41:1595:89265:22:22:71:539:556:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:andu0=9%.  The series on resources devoted to matching constructed byLandais,  Michaillat
41:1596:89354:22:21:71:539:534:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and Saez(2015) indicate that when the unemployment rate is around 9%,  as in 2009:Q2,  then
41:1597:89445:21:40:71:337:513:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:τ=1.7%. So we setτ0=1.7%. Under this calibration,
41:1598:89494:40:0:71:198:473:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:(36)m0=
41:1599:89501:0:16:266:279:481:12:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:M0
41:1600:89503:16:0:203:342:465:12:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:1−0.165×2×(1.7/9)×M0
41:1601:89523:0:0:347:356:473:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:=
41:1602:89524:0:16:390:403:481:12:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:M0
41:1603:89526:16:0:360:432:465:12:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:1+0.062×M0
41:1604:89536:0:40:435:438:473:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:.
41:1605:89537:40:21:89:539:433:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The unemployment multiplierM0is estimated by measuring the response of the unemployment
41:1606:89624:21:22:72:540:412:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:rate (in percentage points) when government purchases increase by 1% of GDP. Monacelli, Perotti
41:1607:89719:22:22:72:539:390:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and Trigari(2010) estimate a structural vector autoregression (SVAR) on US data for 1954–2006
41:1608:89812:22:21:72:540:368:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and find unemployment multipliers between 0.2 and 0.6, depending on how the multiplier is de-
41:1609:89905:21:22:72:540:347:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fined.Ramey(2013) estimates SVARs on US data for 1939–2008.  All the identification schemes
41:1610:89996:22:22:72:540:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and sample periods considered give unemployment multipliers between 0.2 and 0.5, except one
41:1611:90087:22:21:72:540:303:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:specification giving an unemployment multiplier of 1.23As discussed byBarro and Redlick(2011),
41:1612:90181:21:22:72:540:282:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:one potential issue is that these multipliers are estimated using deficit-financed increases in gov-
41:1613:90281:22:22:72:540:260:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ernment purchases, not balanced-budget increases.  This issue is not very important here because
41:1614:90377:22:21:72:540:238:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:unemployment multipliers are larger once the negative response of labor supply to distortionary
41:1615:90472:21:22:72:540:217:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:taxes is taken into account.  This is because a reduction in labor supply leads to higher tightness
41:1616:90571:22:22:72:540:195:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and lower unemployment in the matching model (Michaillat and Saez 2015).  Hence, these esti-
41:1617:90663:22:18:72:432:173:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:mates are a lower bound for the balanced-budget unemployment multiplier.
41:1618:90735:18:12:82:424:155:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:21The caseε=1 corresponds to a Cobb-Douglas utility function:U(c,g) =c1−γ·gγ.
41:1619:90812:12:16:82:540:143:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:22The theoretical multiplierm0is difficult to directly estimate because it measures the response to a change in
41:1620:90923:16:12:71:540:127:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:government consumptiong, which is government purchasesGminus the resources devoted by the government for
41:1621:91027:12:12:71:540:115:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:matching and therefore difficult to observe. The empirical multiplierM0is much easier to estimate because it measures
41:1622:91144:12:8:71:444:103:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the response to a change in government purchasesG, which are reported in national accounts.
41:1623:91235:8:0:82:427:95:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:23See Monacelli, Perotti and Trigari (2010, pp.533–536) and Ramey (2013, pp.40–42).
42:1624:91320:0:22:89:540:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We  can  also  measure  the  unemployment  multiplierM0from  estimates  of  the  output  multi-
42:1625:91415:22:22:71:539:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:plier obtained under deficit financing.  Indeed, under the standard assumption that households are
42:1626:91513:22:21:71:539:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Ricardian, deficit financing is equivalent to lump-sum taxation.  Then, under the typical assump-
42:1627:91610:21:22:71:540:643:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tion that the utility functionU(c,g)is separable, changes in government purchases financed with
42:1628:91705:22:22:71:539:621:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:lump-sum taxation have no effect on the labor supply.  Therefore, unemployment multiplier and
42:1629:91798:22:21:71:540:599:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:output multipliers are the same (Proposition10).24Ramey(2011, Table 1) reports that in aggre-
42:1630:91891:21:22:71:539:578:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:gate analyses on postwar US data, deficit-financed output multipliers are between 0.6 and 1.6. This
42:1631:91990:22:22:71:539:556:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:evidence indicates that when the tax changes used to finance changes in government purchases are
42:1632:92086:22:21:71:440:534:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:nondistortionary, the unemployment multiplier could be in the 0.6–1.6 range.
42:1633:92162:21:22:89:539:513:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Overall, the average unemployment multiplier is likely to fall in the 0.2–1.6 range.  If multi-
42:1634:92257:22:22:71:539:491:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:pliers are larger when unemployment is higher, as suggested by several articles computing state-
42:1635:92353:22:21:71:539:469:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:dependent multipliers on US data,M0could even be larger.25Given the uncertainty about the exact
42:1636:92448:21:22:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:estimate of the unemployment multiplier, we compute the optimal level of stimulus spending for
42:1637:92542:22:22:72:170:426:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:M0between 0 and 2.
42:1638:92560:22:21:89:539:404:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The  graph  on  the  left  in  Figure2  displays  the  optimal  level  of  government  purchases  as  a
42:1639:92663:21:22:71:539:383:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:share of output,G/Y,  as a function of the initial unemployment multiplier,M0.   This graph is
42:1640:92757:22:22:72:539:361:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:constructed using (20).  Initially the unemployment rate isu0=9%, but with the optimal policy
42:1641:92850:22:21:72:539:339:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the unemployment rate falls below its initial level. The graph on the right in Figure2 displays the
42:1642:92949:21:22:72:540:318:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:unemployment rate that prevails once government purchases have been adjusted to their optimal
42:1643:93042:22:22:72:277:296:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:level. This graph is constructed using (21).
42:1644:93086:22:21:89:539:274:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The numerical application illustrates all the theoretical results obtained in the previous sections.
42:1645:93186:21:22:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In addition, it provides orders of magnitude for the optimal response of government purchases to a
42:1646:93284:22:22:72:394:231:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:realistic increase in unemployment. Several observations stand out.
42:1647:93351:22:22:89:539:209:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A first observation is that even with a small multiplier of 0.2, government purchases should
42:1648:93443:22:21:72:540:187:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:increase  significantly  above  the  Samuelson  level  in  response  to  the  increase  in  unemployment
42:1649:93547:21:22:72:539:166:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:from 6% to 9%. Withε=0.5, government purchases should increase by 1.5 percentage points of
42:1650:93637:22:19:72:540:144:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:GDP toG/Y=18.0%.  Forε=1, they should increase by 2.8 points of GDP toG/Y=19.3%.
42:1651:93717:19:15:82:539:125:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:24If the utility function is not separable, the unemployment and output multipliers are not exactly the same because
42:1652:93833:15:9:72:501:110:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f4:dk/dg6=0 (see equation (29) withτL=0). But they are close as long as the effect of g on∂U/∂cis small.
42:1653:93934:9:15:82:539:101:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:25SeeAuerbach and Gorodnichenko(2012),Candelon and Lieb(2013), andFazzari, Morley and Panovska(2015).
42:1654:94035:15:0:72:472:86:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Auerbach and Gorodnichenko(2012, Table 1, row 3) report output multipliers above 2 in recessions.

43:1675:94285:159:14:81:529:526:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figure 2: Optimal Government Purchases, and Unemployment Rate under the Optimal Policy
43:1676:94371:14:12:72:540:512:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:Notes:In 2008:Q3 in the United States, the unemployment rate wasu=6% and government purchases wereG/Y=
43:1677:94473:12:12:72:539:500:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:16.5%. We consider that the labor market was efficient and government purchases were optimal in 2008:Q3. The Great
43:1678:94587:12:12:72:540:488:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Recession shock hit the US economy around that time. The unemployment rate was projected to increase to 9% after
43:1679:94699:12:12:72:540:476:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:the shock. The graph on the left displays the optimal response of government purchases, expressed as a share of output,
43:1680:94818:12:12:72:540:464:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:after the shock. The optimal response is computed using (20),u∗=6%,(G/Y)∗=16.5%,u0=9%,η=0.6,εequal
43:1681:94916:12:12:71:539:452:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:to 0.5, 1, and 2,M0between 0 and 2, and the facts thatM0andm0are linked by (36) andG/Y=G/C/(1+G/C). The
43:1682:95019:12:12:71:539:440:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:graph on the right displays the unemployment rate once government purchases are set optimally. The unemployment
43:1683:95130:12:34:71:285:428:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:rate is computed using (21) with the same calibration.
43:1684:95184:34:22:71:540:394:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:And forε=2, they should increase by 4.6 points of GDP toG/Y=21.1%.  Thus, the optimal
43:1685:95269:22:22:71:390:372:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:level of stimulus spending is quite large even for small multipliers.
43:1686:95338:22:21:89:539:350:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A second observation is that the unemployment multiplier that warrants the largest increase in
43:1687:95432:21:22:71:540:329:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:government purchases is fairly modest. Withε=0.5, the largest increase is 2.6 percentage points
43:1688:95527:22:22:71:539:307:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of GDP and it occurs with a multiplier of 0.6. Withε=1, the largest increase is 3.6 points of GDP
43:1689:95624:22:21:71:540:285:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and it occurs with a multiplier of 0.4. And withε=2, the largest increase is 5 points of GDP and
43:1690:95720:21:22:71:228:264:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:it occurs with a multiplier of 0.3.
43:1691:95755:22:22:89:539:242:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A third observation is that optimal government purchases are the same for small and large mul-
43:1692:95849:22:21:71:540:220:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tipliers.  For instance, fixε=1.  The optimal increase in government purchases is the same for
43:1693:95943:21:22:71:539:199:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:multipliers of 0.12 and 1.5—1.9 points of GDP. The optimal increase in government purchases is
43:1694:96037:22:22:71:539:177:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:also the same for multipliers of 0.08 and 2—1.3 points of GDP. Of course the resulting unemploy-
43:1695:96133:22:21:71:539:155:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ment rates are very different. The optimal policy fills a much larger portion of the unemployment
43:1696:96230:21:22:71:200:134:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:gap with a large multiplier.
43:1697:96258:22:22:89:539:112:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A fourth observation is that, even though government purchases increase significantly for small
43:1698:96353:22:0:71:539:90:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:multipliers, the unemployment rate barely falls below its initial level of 9%.  With the multiplier
44:1699:96454:0:22:72:539:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of 0.2, the unemployment rate only falls to 8.7% withε=0.5, to 8.5% withε=1, and to 8.1%
44:1700:96542:22:22:72:539:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:withε=2. Unemployment does not fall much because government purchases have little effect on
44:1701:96633:22:21:72:283:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:unemployment when the multiplier is small.
44:1702:96675:21:22:89:539:643:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A fifth observation is that, with a multiplier above 1, the stabilization of the unemployment
44:1703:96768:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:rate is almost perfect.  With a multiplier of 1, the unemployment rate achieved with the optimal
44:1704:96864:22:21:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:policy is below 6.8%, so the remaining unemployment gap is less than 0.8 percentage points. With
44:1705:96960:21:22:72:480:578:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:a multiplier of 2, the remaining unemployment gap is less than 0.2 percentage points.
44:1706:97045:22:22:89:540:556:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A last observation is the elasticity of substitution between public and private consumption,ε,
44:1707:97139:22:21:71:539:534:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:plays a significant role for small to medium multipliers but not for large multipliers. Consider first
44:1708:97241:21:22:71:539:513:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:a multiplier to 0.4. Withε=0.5, government purchases should increase by 2.4 percentage points
44:1709:97334:22:22:71:539:491:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of GDP. Withε=1, government purchases should increase by an additional 1.2 points of GDP.
44:1710:97423:22:21:71:540:469:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:And withε=2, government purchases should increase by yet another 1.2 points of GDP. Hence,
44:1711:97513:21:22:71:540:448:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:εsignificantly influences the optimal response of government purchases to unemployment fluctu-
44:1712:97607:22:22:71:539:426:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ations.  On the other hand, for a multiplier above 1, the optimal levels of government purchases
44:1713:97703:22:21:71:540:404:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:forε=0.5,ε=1, andε=2 are nearly indistinguishable.  This is because the optimal policy is
44:1714:97792:21:22:71:539:383:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:broadly to fill the unemployment gap for large multipliers, so the elasticity of substitution has little
44:1715:97896:22:45:71:267:361:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:influence on the optimal policy response.
44:1716:97937:45:34:257:355:316:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:7.  Simulations
44:1717:97952:34:21:71:539:282:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:This section simulates the matching model with land described in Section2.  The model is cal-
44:1718:98045:21:22:71:539:261:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ibrated to US data.  The section serves several purposes.  First, it relates the sufficient statistics
44:1719:98147:22:22:71:539:239:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in the formulas, especially the unemployment multiplier, to parameters of the model.  Second, it
44:1720:98243:22:21:71:539:217:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:demonstrates that the matching model provides a good description of the business cycle:  in re-
44:1721:98338:21:22:71:539:196:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:sponse to aggregate demand shocks, the model generates realistic countercyclical fluctuations in
44:1722:98434:22:22:71:539:174:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the unemployment rate and unemployment multiplier. Third, it confirms that the explicit formula,
44:1723:98530:22:21:71:419:152:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:given by (20), is accurate even for sizable fluctuations in unemployment.
44:1724:98603:21:0:89:539:131:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We begin by specifying the utility function and price mechanism used in the simulations.  We
45:1725:98697:0:40:72:334:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:use a constant-elasticity-of-substitution utility function

45:1727:98763:0:13:256:262:681:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:[

45:1739:98978:22:22:89:539:585:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We use a price mechanism that extends the efficient price mechanism to match empirical evi-
45:1740:99069:22:21:71:539:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:dence on unemployment fluctuations and the unemployment multiplier. The efficient price mech-
45:1741:99162:21:22:71:539:542:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:anismp∗(g)is the price of services ensuring that unemployment is efficient. Using equation (10),
45:1742:99258:22:22:71:124:520:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:we see that

45:1744:99276:0:16:274:280:506:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:1

45:1746:99284:0:0:302:320:498:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:·α·

45:1748:99289:16:0:327:339:490:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f5:∂c

45:1750:99300:31:22:72:540:467:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:whereα≡δ/V′(l0)parameterizes aggregate demand.  If the price is continuously atp∗, the un-
45:1751:99390:22:21:72:539:445:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:employment rate stays atu∗.  Asu∗remains the same in response to aggregate demand or supply
45:1752:99481:21:22:72:540:424:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:shocks,  then unemployment rate remains constant in response to typical business-cycle shocks.
45:1753:99575:22:22:72:540:402:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Furthermore, since the unemployment rate remains atu∗whengchanges, the unemployment mul-
45:1754:99663:22:21:72:540:380:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tiplier is zero.  However, the unemployment multiplier is positive (see Section6), and unemploy-
45:1755:99759:21:22:72:540:359:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ment is subject to wide business-cycle fluctuations.  To introduce unemployment fluctuations and
45:1756:99855:22:41:72:496:337:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:a positive multiplier, we consider a price mechanism less flexible than the efficient price:
45:1757:99947:41:0:72:291:296:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f8:(37)p(g) =p0·α1−r0·
45:1758:99966:0:8:293:302:312:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:(
45:1759:99967:8:17:303:321:304:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f25:∂U
45:1760:99969:17:0:307:319:287:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f5:∂c
45:1761:99971:0:0:326:375:296:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:(y∗−g,g)
45:1762:99979:0:16:375:401:312:12:g_d0_f11:7:g_d0_f4:)1−r1
45:1763:99984:16:40:404:407:296:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:.
45:1764:99985:40:22:71:539:256:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The parameterp0>0 governs the price level. The parameterr0∈[0,1]measures the rigidity of the
45:1765:100077:22:21:71:539:234:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:price with respect to aggregate demand: ifr0=1, the price does not respond to aggregate demand;
45:1766:100172:21:22:71:540:213:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ifr0=0, the price responds as much to aggregate demand as the efficient price.  The parameter
45:1767:100265:22:22:71:540:191:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:r1∈[0,1]measures the rigidity of the price with respect to the marginal utility of private services:
45:1768:100365:22:21:71:539:169:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ifr1=1, the price does not respond to shocks to the marginal utility; ifr1=0, the price responds
45:1769:100461:21:22:71:320:148:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:as much to the marginal utility as the efficient price.
45:1770:100516:22:22:89:539:126:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Calibratingr0>0 allows aggregate demand shocks to generate inefficient fluctuations in un-
45:1771:100606:22:21:71:539:104:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:employment. Calibratingr1>0 allows for a positive unemployment multiplier. Indeed,Appendix
45:1772:100696:21:0:71:540:83:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Dshows that the multiplier evaluated with efficient unemployment and government purchases at
46:1773:100790:0:40:72:179:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the Samuelson level is
46:1774:100812:40:0:72:272:668:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:(38)M=
46:1775:100818:0:16:312:320:676:12:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:r1
46:1776:100820:16:0:276:357:660:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f6:r1·γ+ε·(1−γ)
46:1777:100832:0:40:358:361:668:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:.
46:1778:100833:40:21:71:539:628:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Whenr1>0, the multiplier is positive, and the value of the multiplier critically depends onr1. The
46:1779:100931:21:22:71:539:607:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:value of the multiplier also depends on the parametersεandγfrom the utility function, because
46:1780:101024:22:22:71:399:585:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:these parameters influence the shape of the aggregate demand curve.
46:1781:101091:22:21:89:539:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The calibration of the model is standard and relegated to Appendix E. The most important
46:1782:101179:21:22:71:539:542:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:parameters are those determining the sufficient statistics in our formulas. We set these parameters
46:1783:101278:22:22:71:539:520:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:such  thatε=1,u∗=6.1%  (average  unemployment  rate  in  the  United  States  for  1990–2014),
46:1784:101372:22:21:71:540:498:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f4:(G/C)∗=19.7% (averageG/Cin the United States for 1990–2014),η=0.6 (Landais, Michaillat
46:1785:101458:21:22:71:501:477:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and Saez 2015), andM=0.5 (midrange of the multiplier estimates for the United States).
46:1786:101544:22:22:89:539:455:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We represent the business cycle as a succession of unexpected permanent aggregate demand
46:1787:101632:22:21:71:539:433:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:shocks.   We parameterize aggregate demand withα=δ/V′(l0).   Since the economy jumps to
46:1788:101719:21:22:71:539:412:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:its new steady-state equilibrium in response to an unexpected permanent shock, we only need to
46:1789:101813:22:22:71:539:390:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:compute a collection of steady states parameterized by different values ofα. We perform two sets
46:1790:101909:22:21:71:539:368:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of simulations: one in whichG/Yremains constant at 16.5%, its average value in the United States
46:1791:102005:21:22:71:466:347:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:for 1990–2014, and one in whichG/Yis always at its optimal level, given by (12).
46:1792:102085:22:22:89:540:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figure3 displays the results of the simulations. Each equilibrium is indexed byα∈[0.97,1.03].
46:1793:102178:22:21:71:540:303:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The equilibria with lowαrepresent slumps: the price of services is high and unemployment is high.
46:1794:102275:21:22:71:540:282:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The equilibria with highαrepresent booms: the price of services is low and unemployment is low.
46:1795:102370:22:22:71:540:260:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:WhenG/Yremains constant at 16.5%, the unemployment rate rises from 4.4% whenα=1.3, to
46:1796:102455:22:21:71:401:238:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:its efficient level of 6.1% whenα=1, and to 11.0% whenα=0.97.
46:1797:102516:21:22:89:539:217:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The unemployment multiplier is sharply countercyclical, increasing from 0.2 to 1.4 when the
46:1798:102607:22:22:71:539:195:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:unemployment rate increases from 4.4% to 11.0%. This sharp increase of the multiplier is consis-
46:1799:102703:22:21:71:539:173:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tent with recent evidence based on aggregate US data provided that multipliers are higher when
46:1800:102797:21:22:71:540:152:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:unemployment is higher or output is lower.26The mechanism behind the countercyclicality of the
46:1801:102891:22:18:71:540:130:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:multiplier is described byMichaillat(2014).  When unemployment is high, there is a lot of idle
46:1802:102985:18:16:82:540:112:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:26See  for  instanceAuerbach  and  Gorodnichenko(2012),Candelon  and  Lieb(2013),  andFazzari,  Morley  and
46:1803:103092:16:12:71:539:96:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Panovska(2015).  On the other hand,Owyang, Ramey and Zubairy(2013) find that multipliers in the United States
46:1804:103201:12:0:71:290:84:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:are not necessarily larger when the economy is slacker.
47:1805:103258:0:14:133:261:570:4:Times:4:Times:0.9811.02
47:1806:103267:14:0:146:247:556:5:g_d0_f36:5:g_d0_f36:Aggregate demand

47:1810:103292:0:0:91:112:672:4:Times:4:Times:10%

47:1812:103315:10:12:208:270:694:4:g_d0_f36:4:g_d0_f37:ConstantG=Y
47:1813:103326:12:112:208:266:682:4:g_d0_f36:4:g_d0_f37:OptimalG=Y

47:1831:103497:112:14:368:497:401:4:Times:4:Times:0.9811.02
47:1832:103506:14:0:382:483:387:5:g_d0_f40:5:g_d0_f40:Aggregate demand
47:1833:103522:0:0:327:348:410:4:Times:4:Times:13%
47:1834:103525:0:0:327:348:441:4:Times:4:Times:15%
47:1835:103528:0:0:327:348:472:4:Times:4:Times:17%
47:1836:103531:0:0:327:348:503:4:Times:4:Times:19%
47:1837:103534:0:10:327:348:535:4:Times:4:Times:21%
47:1838:103559:10:12:437:496:525:4:g_d0_f40:4:g_d0_f37:OptimalG=Y
47:1839:103569:12:155:437:509:513:4:g_d0_f40:4:g_d0_f40:Explicit formula
47:1840:103585:155:14:109:502:358:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figure3: Simulations of Optimal Government Purchases Over the Business Cycle
47:1841:103661:14:12:72:540:344:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f4:Notes:The simulation model is a general-equilibrium matching model with land, described in Section7. The model is
47:1842:103774:12:12:72:539:332:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:calibrated inAppendix E. The business cycle is generated by varying the level of aggregate demand. A low aggregate
47:1843:103888:12:12:72:540:320:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:demand level means a high marginal utility of holding land or a low time discount factor. The simulations compare an
47:1844:104004:12:12:72:539:308:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:economy where government purchases are constant atG/Y=16.5% to an economy where government purchases are
47:1845:104108:12:12:72:540:296:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:set optimally using formula (12). In the top right graph, the unemployment multiplier is the empirical unemployment
47:1846:104223:12:12:72:540:284:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:multiplier defined by (32).  In the bottom right graph, the solid green line displays the government purchases given
47:1847:104339:12:34:72:277:272:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:by (20) and the dashed red line those given by (12).
47:1848:104391:34:21:72:540:238:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:capacity so the matching process is congested by sellers of services.  Hence, an increase in gov-
47:1849:104488:21:22:72:540:217:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ernment purchases has very little effect on other buyers of services.  Crowding out of household
47:1850:104584:22:22:72:461:195:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:purchases by government purchases is therefore weak, and the multiplier is large.
47:1851:104665:22:21:89:539:173:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The model is calibrated so that the unemployment rate is efficient whenα=1.  Hence, the
47:1852:104752:21:22:71:540:152:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:unemployment rate is inefficiently high whenα<1 and inefficiently low whenα>1.   Since
47:1853:104838:22:22:71:539:130:12:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f8:the unemployment multiplier is positive, the government purchases ratio should be above(G/Y)∗
47:1854:104931:22:21:71:539:108:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:whenα<1 and below whenα>1. Indeed, optimal government purchases is markedly counter-
47:1855:105015:21:0:71:522:87:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cyclical, decreasing fromG/Y=20.4% toG/Y=13.7% whenαincreases from 0.97 to 1.03.
48:1856:105097:0:22:89:539:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Unemployment  responds  to  the  adjustment  of  government  purchases  to  their  optimal  level.
48:1857:105195:22:22:72:539:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Whenα<1, optimal government purchases are higher thanG/Y=16.5% so unemployment is
48:1858:105276:22:21:72:539:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:below its original level.  For instance, atα=0.97 the unemployment rate falls by 3.8 percentage
48:1859:105371:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:points from 11.0% to 7.2%. Whenα>1, optimal government purchases are belowG/Y=16.5%
48:1860:105454:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:so unemployment is above its original level.  For instance,  atα=1.03 the unemployment rate
48:1861:105545:22:21:72:328:599:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:increases by 0.8 percentage point from 4.4% to 5.2%.
48:1862:105597:21:22:89:539:578:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Finally, the simulations show that the explicit formula, given by (20), is quite accurate.  For-
48:1863:105693:22:22:72:540:556:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:mula (20) is valid up to a second-order remainder.  Since the unemployment rate displays large
48:1864:105787:22:21:72:540:534:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fluctuations, there is a risk that the remainder is large and the approximation given by the formula
48:1865:105887:21:22:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:inaccurate. In our simulations, however, this does not happen. The government purchases obtained
48:1866:105983:22:22:72:539:491:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:with the approximate explicit formula and the exact formula are close. Atα=1, the two formulas
48:1867:106077:22:21:71:539:469:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:gives the sameG/Y. Whenαis further away from 1, the approximation remains satisfactory. The
48:1868:106168:21:22:71:540:448:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:deviation between exact and explicit formula is always below one percentage point: atα=1.03,
48:1869:106260:22:22:71:540:426:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the exact formula givesG/Y=13.7% while the explicit formula givesG/Y=14.6%; atα=0.97,
48:1870:106345:22:45:72:482:404:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the exact formula givesG/Y=20.4% while the explicit formula givesG/Y=19.7%.
48:1871:106420:45:33:259:353:359:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:8.  Conclusion
48:1872:106434:33:22:72:540:326:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:This paper presents a simplified theory of optimal government purchases.  The theory clarifies a
48:1873:106530:22:22:72:456:304:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:number of existing ideas about the use of government spending for stabilization.
48:1874:106610:22:21:89:539:282:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A first idea is that stimulus spending in slumps is desirable if the output multiplier is above one
48:1875:106709:21:22:72:540:261:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(as in traditional Keynesian models). Indeed, with an output multiplier above one, public consump-
48:1876:106807:22:22:72:540:239:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tion crowds in private consumption, so additional public consumption improves welfare.  While
48:1877:106900:22:21:72:540:217:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:crowding in is obviously a sufficient condition to justify stimulus spending, it is absolutely not a
48:1878:107000:21:22:72:540:196:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:necessary condition.  In our theory, public consumption always crowds out private consumption;
48:1879:107094:22:22:72:540:174:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:nevertheless, stimulus spending is desirable in slumps whenever the unemployment multiplier is
48:1880:107188:22:21:72:540:152:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:positive—so that an increase in government spending reduces the unemployment rate. This result
48:1881:107282:21:22:72:540:131:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:holds both whether taxes are distortionary or not.  Since available estimates of the unemployment
48:1882:107379:22:22:72:436:109:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:multiplier are positive, stimulus spending is likely to be desirable in slumps.
48:1883:107458:22:0:89:539:87:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A concern of stimulus skeptics is that multipliers are estimated using deficit-financed increases
49:1884:107557:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in  government  purchases,  not  balanced-budget  increases,  and  that  balanced-budget  and  deficit-
49:1885:107660:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:financed multipliers may have opposite sign.  For instance, Barro and Redlick (2011) find in US
49:1886:107755:22:21:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:data that the deficit-financed output multiplier is positive but the balanced-budget output multi-
49:1887:107853:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:plier is negative. The mechanism is that higher government purchases require higher distortionary
49:1888:107950:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:taxes, which depress output through negative labor-supply responses.  Our theory alleviates this
49:1889:108046:22:21:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:concern, however.  It is not the output multiplier but the unemployment multiplier that should be
49:1890:108143:21:22:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:used to design optimal stimulus spending. While the output multiplier is smaller and can become
49:1891:108238:22:22:72:540:556:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:negative once tax distortions are taken into account, the unemployment multiplier is larger once
49:1892:108334:22:21:72:540:534:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tax distortions are taken into account.  This is because a reduction in labor supply leads to lower
49:1893:108433:21:22:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:output but higher tightness and lower unemployment in the matching model (Michaillat and Saez
49:1894:108526:22:22:72:540:491:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:2015).  In fact, the unemployment multiplier equals the output multiplier net of the labor-supply
49:1895:108623:22:21:72:540:469:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:responses due to distortionary taxation.  With strong negative labor-supply responses, a negative
49:1896:108720:21:22:72:409:448:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:output multiplier can coexist with a positive unemployment multiplier.
49:1897:108790:22:22:89:539:426:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our theory also links the optimal level of stimulus spending to the size of the unemployment
49:1898:108882:22:21:72:540:404:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:multiplier.  Stimulus skeptics usually believe in small multipliers and infer that stimulus spending
49:1899:108982:21:22:72:540:383:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:should be small or zero in slumps. On the other hand, stimulus advocates usually believe in large
49:1900:109079:22:22:72:540:361:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:multipliers and infer that stimulus spending should be large in slumps.  In fact, our theory shows
49:1901:109177:22:21:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that the relationship between the optimal level of stimulus spending and the size of the unemploy-
49:1902:109275:21:22:72:540:318:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ment multiplier is hump-shaped. In a US calibration, the relationship peaks for an unemployment
49:1903:109370:22:22:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:multiplier of 0.4. So a multiplier of 0.4 calls for the highest level of stimulus spending. Higher and
49:1904:109472:22:21:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:lower multipliers warrant smaller levels, such that the optimal level of stimulus spending is similar
49:1905:109573:21:22:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:for small and large multipliers.  For instance, in our US calibration, the optimal level of stimulus
49:1906:109673:22:22:72:390:231:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:spending is the same for unemployment multipliers of 0.1 and 1.8.
49:1907:109738:22:22:89:539:209:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Next, our theory links the optimal level of stimulus spending to the usefulness of additional
49:1908:109831:22:21:72:540:187:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:public spending.  A concern of stimulus skeptics is that additional government spending could be
49:1909:109927:21:22:72:540:166:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:wasteful.   Our theory develops this argument.   It is true that when the elasticity of substitution
49:1910:110027:22:22:72:540:144:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:between  public  and  private  consumption  is  zero,  so  that  additional  public  workers  dig  and  fill
49:1911:110135:22:21:72:540:122:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:holes in the ground, government purchases should remain at the Samuelson level and not be used
49:1912:110229:21:22:72:540:101:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:for stabilization. But in the more realistic case where the elasticity of substitution is positive, some
49:1913:110333:22:0:72:540:79:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:stimulus spending is desirable in slumps.  We also qualify the view of stimulus advocates in the
50:1914:110431:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Keynesian tradition who argue that government purchases should entirely fill the unemployment
50:1915:110524:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:gap, irrespective of the usefulness of additional public spending. It is true that when the elasticity
50:1916:110626:22:21:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of substitution is infinite, so that public and private consumption are perfect substitute, government
50:1917:110728:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:purchases should completely fill the unemployment gap.  But in the more realistic case where the
50:1918:110824:22:22:72:517:621:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:elasticity is finite, government purchases fill the unemployment gap partially, not completely.
50:1919:110919:22:21:89:539:599:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Overall,  government  purchases  could  contribute  to  stabilization  whenever  monetary  policy
50:1920:111016:21:22:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is constrained.   This situation arises when the zero lower bound on the nominal interest rate is
50:1921:111113:22:22:72:540:556:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:binding—for instance, in the United States, Japan, and the European Union in the aftermath of the
50:1922:111210:22:21:72:540:534:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Great Recession. This situation also applies to members of a monetary union, which have no con-
50:1923:111305:21:22:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:trol over monetary policy but can tailor government purchases and taxes to local conditions—for
50:1924:111400:22:22:72:540:491:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:instance, a country in the eurozone or a state in the United States. Furthermore, since it focuses on
50:1925:111501:22:21:72:540:469:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:budget-balanced government purchases, our theory is particularly appropriate for US states, which
50:1926:111598:21:36:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cannot run budget deficits, and eurozone countries, which face strict limits on their budget deficits.

54:2069:121517:0:26:75:536:707:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:Appendix A.  The Absence of Transitional Dynamics on the Labor Market
54:2070:121586:26:15:72:540:681:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In the analysis, we abstract from transitional dynamics for the unemployment rate and output.  In
54:2071:121683:15:14:72:540:666:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:this appendix we use labor market data for the US to validate this approximation.  We show that
54:2072:121778:14:15:72:389:652:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the transitional dynamics of the unemployment rate are negligible.
54:2073:121844:15:14:89:540:637:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We begin by constructing a time series for the selling rateft.  We measure one unit of service
54:2074:121938:14:15:72:540:623:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:by one job, so that the selling rate is a job-finding rate. We assume that unemployed workers find a
54:2075:122038:15:14:72:539:608:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:job according to a Poisson process with arrival rateft. Thus, the monthly job-finding rate satisfies
54:2076:122138:14:14:73:539:594:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:ft=−ln(1−Ft), whereFtis the monthly job-finding probability.  We construct a time series for
54:2077:122230:14:33:72:444:580:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:Ftfollowing the method developed by Shimer (2012). We use the relationship
54:2078:122304:33:0:254:295:547:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f8:Ft=1−

54:2085:122592:14:14:72:540:472:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:to four weeks duration, adjusted as inShimer(2012) during the 1994–2014 period.  FigureA1,

54:2103:123364:14:29:89:516:281:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Finally, we compare the actual unemployment rate to the steady-state unemployment rate
54:2104:123450:29:0:71:297:252:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:(A1)ut=

54:2109:123564:14:37:71:431:206:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the transitional dynamics of the actual unemployment rate are unimportant.
54:2110:123638:37:15:82:539:169:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:27One concern is that increases in government purchases cannot be undone because jobs created by the government
54:2111:123749:15:12:72:540:154:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:are effectively permanent.  It is true that government jobs separate more slowly than private jobs.  Using data con-
54:2112:123865:12:12:72:540:142:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:structed by the BLS from the Job Opening and Labor Turnover Survey for 2000–2014, we find that the average monthly
54:2113:123979:12:12:72:540:130:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:separation rate is 3.9% for private jobs and 1.4% for government jobs.  Nevertheless, the separation rate for govern-
54:2114:124096:12:12:72:540:118:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:ment jobs remains sizable. If no new jobs were created by the government, the level of government purchases would
54:2115:124209:12:12:72:539:106:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:rapidly decrease. Indeed, with a hiring freeze, US government employment would fall by 1−exp(−0.014·12) =15%
54:2116:124317:12:0:72:118:94:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:in one year.

55:2151:125601:35:27:80:531:114:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:Appendix B.  Demand Structure and Price Mechanism: Other Examples
55:2152:125666:27:14:71:539:87:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In this appendix we present three other examples of demand structure and price mechanism for the
55:2153:125762:14:0:71:540:73:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:matching model of Section2. These examples yield the same equilibrium structure as the example
56:2154:125858:0:15:72:229:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:with land described in Section 2.
56:2155:125891:15:14:89:539:693:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:First, the variablel(t)in the land model can be interpreted as a generic unproduced good, as in
56:2156:125986:14:15:71:477:679:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Hart (1982). It could also be interpreted as a specific unproduced good, such as gold.
56:2157:126072:15:14:89:539:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Second, the land model could be slightly modified by replacing land by money and assuming
56:2158:126161:14:15:71:539:650:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that households derive utility from holding real money balances.  Introducing money in the utility
56:2159:126259:15:14:71:540:635:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:function is a classical way to generate an aggregate demand.  FollowingSidrauski(1967), a large
56:2160:126354:14:15:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:number of business-cycle models with money in the utility function have been developed.  Two
56:2161:126446:15:14:72:539:606:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:prominent examples areBarro and Grossman(1971) andBlanchard and Kiyotaki(1987).  Money
56:2162:126532:14:14:72:531:592:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is introduced in the utility function to capture the fact that money helps conducting transactions.
56:2163:126631:14:15:89:540:578:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In the money model, a household holdsM(t)units of money and the supply of money is fixed
56:2164:126719:15:14:71:540:563:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:atM0.  In equilibrium, the money market clears andM(t) =M0.  The price of services in terms of
56:2165:126813:14:15:72:539:549:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:money isp(t). We specify a general price mechanism that determines the price of services:p(t) =
56:2166:126908:15:14:72:540:534:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:p(g(t)).   The household’s instantaneous utility function isU(c(t),g(t)) +V(M(t)/p(t)).   The
56:2167:127001:14:15:71:539:520:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f8:law of motion of the household’s real money balancesm(t)≡M(t)/p(t)is   ̇m(t) = (1−u(x(t)))·
56:2168:127092:15:14:71:540:505:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:k−(1+τ(x(t)))·c(t)−π(t)·m(t)−T(t), whereπ(t)≡ ̇p(t)/p(t)is the inflation rate.  In steady
56:2169:127181:14:15:72:539:491:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:state,gand thuspare fixed so inflation is zero. The equilibrium immediately converges to steady
56:2170:127276:15:14:72:539:476:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f8:state.  In steady state the desired private consumptionc(x,p,g)is given by∂U/∂c= (1+τ(x))·
56:2171:127366:14:14:72:512:462:12:g_d0_f25:12:g_d0_f4:V′(M0/p)/δ. Equilibrium tightnessx(g)is implicitly defined byc(x,g,p(g))+g=y(x,k).
56:2172:127448:14:15:89:539:448:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Third,  the  land  model  could  be  slightly  modified  by  replacing  land  by  nominal  bonds  and
56:2173:127549:15:14:72:540:433:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:assuming that households derive utility from holding real bonds.  Introducing bonds in the utility
56:2174:127647:14:15:72:540:419:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:function is a simple way to generate an aggregate demand in a dynamic economy. It is especially
56:2175:127742:15:14:72:540:404:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:adapted to modern, cashless macroeconomic models. The assumption that wealth enters the utility
56:2176:127837:14:15:72:540:390:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:function has been used in growth models (Kurz 1968;Zou 1994), microeconomic models (Robson
56:2177:127927:15:14:72:540:375:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:1992;Cole, Mailath and Postlewaite 1995), life-cycle models (Carroll 2000;Francis 2009), asset-
56:2178:128022:14:15:72:540:361:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:pricing models (Bakshi and Chen 1996;Gong and Zou 2002), business-cycle models (Michaillat
56:2179:128112:15:14:72:540:346:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and Saez 2014;Ono and Yamada 2014), and public-economics models (Saez and Stantcheva 2016).
56:2180:128203:14:14:72:540:332:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Wealth is introduced in the utility function to capture the fact that people care about wealth not
56:2181:128301:14:15:72:540:318:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:only as future consumption but for its own sake. Wealth could be valued for several reasons: high
56:2182:128398:15:14:72:540:303:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:wealth provides high social status; high wealth provides political power; people value frugality and
56:2183:128498:14:15:72:514:289:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:asceticism and thus dignify the accumulation of wealth; or people value bequeathing wealth.
56:2184:128589:15:14:89:539:274:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In the bond model, bonds are issued and purchased by households, and they have a price of 1
56:2185:128680:14:15:72:540:260:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in terms of money. Money only plays the role of a unit of account. A household holdsB(t)bonds
56:2186:128773:15:14:72:540:245:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and bonds are in zero net supply.  In equilibrium, the bond market clears andB(t) =0.  The rate
56:2187:128868:14:15:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of return on bonds is the nominal interest ratei(t). The nominal interest rate is determined by the
56:2188:128967:15:14:72:539:216:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:central bank, which sets an interest ratei(t) =i(g(t)).  We allow the interest rate to depend on
56:2189:129063:14:15:72:468:202:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:public consumption to allow for an interaction between monetary and fiscal policy.
56:2190:129145:15:14:89:539:187:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The price of services in terms of money isp(t).   The inflation rate isπ(t)≡ ̇p(t)/p(t).   In
56:2191:129238:14:14:72:540:173:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the economy there are two goods—services and bonds—and hence one relative price (public and
56:2192:129329:14:15:72:540:159:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:private services have the same price). The price of bonds relative to services is determined by the
56:2193:129428:15:14:72:540:144:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:real interest rate,i(t)−π(t). Since the nominal interest rate is determined by the central bank, it is
56:2194:129530:14:15:72:540:130:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the inflation rate that determines the real interest rate. The inflation rate is determined by a general
56:2195:129634:15:14:72:539:115:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:price mechanism:π(t) =π(g(t)).  Given the inflation rate, the price of services moves according
56:2196:129729:14:15:72:540:101:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:to   ̇p(t) =π(t)·p(t).  The initial pricep(0)is given.  Given the inflation rate and nominal interest
56:2197:129830:15:14:72:460:86:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:rate, tightness adjusts such that supply equals demand on the market for services.
56:2198:129912:14:0:89:540:72:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The household’s instantaneous utility function isU(c(t),g(t)) +V(B(t)/p(t)).  The law of
57:2199:130002:0:15:72:539:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f8:motion of the household’s real wealthb(t)≡B(t)/p(t)is ̇b(t) = (1−u(x(t)))·k−(1+τ(x(t)))·
57:2200:130090:15:14:72:540:693:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:c(t)+(i(t)−π(t))·b(t)−T(t). As earlier, the equilibrium immediately converges to steady state.
57:2201:130184:14:15:72:539:679:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:In  steady  state,  the  desired  amount  of  private  consumptionc(x,i,π,g)is  given  by∂U/∂c=
57:2202:130279:15:14:72:539:664:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f4:(1+τ(x))·V′(0)/(δ−i+π).  This equation is the usual consumption Euler equation modified
57:2203:130366:14:15:72:540:650:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:by the utility of wealth and evaluated in steady state. The demand for saving arises in part from in-
57:2204:130467:15:14:72:540:635:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tertemporal consumption-smoothing considerations and in part from the utility provided by wealth.
57:2205:130564:14:15:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The equation implies that at the margin, the household is indifferent between consuming and hold-
57:2206:130661:15:36:72:540:606:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ing real wealth. Equilibrium tightnessx(g)is implicitly defined byc(x,i(g),π(g),g)+g=y(x,k).
57:2207:130753:36:26:83:529:570:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:Appendix C.  Properties of the Utility Function in the Simulation Model
57:2208:130824:26:14:72:540:544:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In this appendix we compute the derivatives of the utility function from the simulation model of
57:2209:130920:14:15:72:540:530:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Section7. We use the results to compute the unemployment multiplier inAppendix Dand calibrate
57:2210:131013:15:14:71:194:515:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the model inAppendix E.
57:2211:131036:14:33:89:463:501:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The simulation model has a constant-elasticity-of-substitution utility function:
57:2212:131116:33:0:203:253:468:12:g_d0_f25:12:g_d0_f6:U(c,g) =
57:2213:131124:0:13:256:262:481:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:[
57:2214:131125:13:0:261:295:468:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:(1−γ)
57:2215:131130:0:8:296:299:476:7:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f9:1ε

57:2217:131134:0:8:315:322:476:7:g_d0_f9:7:g_d0_f9:ε−1ε
57:2218:131138:8:0:331:347:468:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f9:+γ
57:2219:131140:0:8:349:352:476:7:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f9:1ε
57:2220:131142:8:0:356:367:468:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f5:·g
57:2221:131144:0:8:368:401:476:7:g_d0_f9:7:g_d0_f4:ε−1ε]εε−1

59:2434:134038:43:26:149:462:388:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:Appendix E.  Calibration of the Simulation Model
59:2435:134086:26:15:71:540:362:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In this appendix we calibrate the simulation model of Section7 based on empirical evidence for
59:2436:134180:15:14:71:489:347:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the United States. The values of the calibrated parameters are summarized in TableA1.
59:2437:134265:14:15:89:539:333:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We begin by calibrating the utility function.   We arbitrarily set the elasticity of substitution
59:2438:134362:15:14:71:539:318:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f9:between public and private consumption toε=1.  As showed inAppendix C, the parameterγ
59:2439:134447:14:15:71:539:304:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:determines the Samuelson level of government purchases:(G/C)∗=γ/(1−γ).  We assume that
59:2440:134533:15:14:71:539:289:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the Samuelson level of government purchases is the average level of government purchases in the
59:2441:134628:14:15:71:505:275:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:United States for 1990–2014:(G/C)∗=19.7% (see Section6). We therefore setγ=0.16.
59:2442:134708:15:14:89:540:260:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Then  we  calibrate  the  matching  parameters.   We  use  the  estimates  ofsandηobtained  by
59:2443:134802:14:14:71:539:246:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Landais, Michaillat and Saez(2015) using US labor market data for 1990–2014:s=2.8% and
59:2444:134888:14:15:71:539:232:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:η=0.6. To calibrate the matching efficacy, we exploit the relationshipu·f(x) =s·(1−u), which
59:2445:134980:15:14:71:540:217:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:impliesω=s·xη−1·(1−u)/u. The average unemployment rate and tightness in US labor market
59:2446:135067:14:15:71:540:203:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:data for 1990–2014 areu=6.1% andx=0.43 (Landais, Michaillat and Saez 2015). Using these
59:2447:135154:15:14:71:540:188:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:average values, we obtainω=0.60.  To calibrate the matching cost, we exploit the relationship
59:2448:135247:14:15:71:539:174:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:τ=ρ·s/[ω·x−η−ρ·s], which impliesρ=ω·x−η·τ/[s·(1+τ)].  This relationship holds for
59:2449:135328:15:14:71:540:159:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:anyτandx, in particular when tightness is efficient sox=x∗andτ=τ∗.  We assume that the
59:2450:135414:14:15:71:539:145:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:efficient unemployment rate and tightness are the average US unemployment rate and tightness
59:2451:135506:15:14:71:540:130:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:for 1990–2014:u∗=6.1% andx∗=0.43.   When tightness is efficient,τ∗=u∗·(1−η)/ηso
59:2452:135585:14:14:71:503:116:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:τ∗=4.1%. Pluggingx∗=0.43 andτ∗=4.1% in the expression forρ, we obtainρ=1.4.
59:2453:135660:14:15:89:539:102:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Last, we calibrate the price mechanism. The empirical evidence suggest that on average in the
59:2454:135753:15:14:71:540:87:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:United States the unemployment multiplier isM=0.5 (see Section6).  Relying on (38), we set
59:2455:135843:14:0:71:539:73:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:r1=0.46 to matchM=0.5.  We calibrate the price level such that when the aggregate demand
60:2456:135933:0:15:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:parameter,α≡δ/V′(l0), equals 1 andG/C= (G/C)∗=19.7%, thenu=u∗=6.1%. Using (37),
60:2457:136012:15:36:72:182:693:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:we find thatp0=0.78.
